O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and entirely abandoned everywhere, therefore its science has perished and been destroyed, and there remains nothing except small descriptions in books that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and foolishness, intentions are closed off, and science is disregarded.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I wish to enliven it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the shapes of the irons for cauterization, and other tools of this work with the arrangement of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of surgery found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And therefore whoever undertakes it must climb up into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and course of veins both moving and resting, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore Hippocrates says that a name without a deed is little, and with a deed it is much.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and indeed in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things said before should guard himself so that he does not fall into error and harm others.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	thus I have seen many times those who meddle with this science and abandon their science and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries in her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	thus so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And another doctor who drew a stone from a man's urine, and the stone was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	So he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to remove it, and saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if he were cut open, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And saw another doctor who took in care Duke our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaking he had a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctor full of ignorance bound the break upon the wound like stars with great carelessness, and left no bandage to the wound, and left him thus at the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commanded that he not untie it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	So that the leg was entirely swollen and the foot, and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come unbind the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I heard it unbound, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all passage for corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the whole limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who drained an inflamed black apostume and then cauterized it out of the malice of his mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	That is to say, surgery where there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	So that foolish doctors may not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Therefore, take your arms with caution, undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and choose the best way so that through God's grace you achieve salvation and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	And leave frightening diseases to those skilled in difficult cures.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove your arms from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his teachings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	'Do not undertake a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical cauteries, ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of instruments, and the irons for cautery, and everything necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, cupping glasses, wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and this chapter is ordered with the forms of instruments
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twisted limbs, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head to the feet, with the forms of instruments
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you about the quality of each temperament and its harm.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of the helper and his harmfulness are a lengthy and subtle science, as well as secret answers;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about this many wise men spoke, and they agreed upon it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	they let me speak few words, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery is generally beneficial to every complexion where there is matter, except two:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	It is to know: hot temperament without matter, and dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry temperament with matter, some people divide it and say that cautery is great help there;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is not useful for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat hot diseases due to heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And he who said the opposite said that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that occur in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	But when you compare the body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it so by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not meddle with fire cautery unless you have experienced it and know well the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of temperaments among men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the conditions and seasonality of the air.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We are not afraid of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians agreed on the use of cauteries.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, son, that fire together with cautery is among the secrets of cures and has greater virtue than a cautery made from burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that is burned, and does no harm to any other member if it could.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Hot medicines spread from member to member by cauterizing, causing painful inflammation in the members;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And by chance, he may kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire alone does not cure unless there is an excess of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experience and the length of service and study that I have put into this art, which is based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And therefore I apologize for the length of my speech, as I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that is hidden in fire and its quality of work, how it overcomes diseases of the body, as philosophers say in their demonstrations.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Or receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be made and chose priests for this purpose.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	I say that cautery is suitable at all times because the harm that arises is kept under control by its aid.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially, cauteries are necessary for immediate and urgent pains which cannot wait until the member suffers greater harm.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish physicians do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	For the disease healed by cautery does not relapse
et il le dient ensi;	And they say thus
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	But it is not so as they believe, for cauteries are no more a medicine that changes complexion and dries the humors causing pain than any other medicine, valued more for its speed of action than for its virtue and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it can happen that the disease comes sometimes according to the constitution of the patient, and the place of the disease and its strength
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, except for cauteries administered where there is little excess or moisture, such as those used for toothache and similar pains, which do not return.
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens rarely
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "derrière" of medicine, and that is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cauteries are valued after medicines, but their intention is false, and cauteries are called the "derrière" of medicine because when we apply various treatments for some diseases and they do not work, then we apply cautery, which is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries of gold are gentler than those of iron; they said this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the place of cautery does not cause decay, but this is not entirely true as I have tested and found it to be so in some men
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauteries of gold are worth more than those of iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	Moreover, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell by its color alone whether it is hot enough; it cools quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much
si font au feu;	one puts it in the fire
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use iron cauteries that we have better prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from top to bottom so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two kinds made:
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine moistening the head for three or four nights, according to what the patient's strength and age and habit can tolerate
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the fire behind the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed-legged between your hands, with his hands on his knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And let where your middle finger comes be the spot to burn with the cautery called 'olivare', of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the marked spot, and move it downwards and outwards, little by little, turning your hand.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then raise your hand gently, and reward yourself if you see a bit of bone appear;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you don't see it, then continue with the cautery until you see the bone as I told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	then take a bit of thread, and place soft cotton inside it, then put it on the spot, leaving it there for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	then put on soft cotton soaked in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the burn is healed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacum" until it is clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, it purges itself more.
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	"And some of these say that one should allow the cautery to burn until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burnt off the bone, and it should be healed."
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should hold the cautery on so long and press it so hard as to abrade bone as thick as a woman's spindle used for spinning, so that the humors flow out more freely.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should dress and bind it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem entirely good to me except in some people where there is room for fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems better to me that I should leave them.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by continuous dissolving of its nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the head of a patient is weak by nature, I find the first type of cautery to be more saving and gentle, and I use this one now together with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	"from the ancient pain of the head"
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When the whole head is afflicted with chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient should use ointments and pills called "cochie," and perform head purging and apply oils and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if one performs the cautery we mentioned earlier, it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Beware if the patient's head is strong in nature and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	In such case, cauterize him a little below the one we mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After performing cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone as we said earlier, perform cautery at the location called "vessels.
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	And this is where cupping glasses are placed.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	And raise your hand so that you do not see down to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much greater pain with this cautery than with others, and I will speak of it elsewhere.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And the cauteries on the horns must be more subtle than those used for cauterizing the middle of the head, and this is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	"of the cautery of the head"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes in a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged by cleansing medications, and all the other treatments I mentioned in the division of illnesses are done, yet nothing helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then make cauteries in two ways, namely with hot water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with hot water is thus: take a pennyworth of aloes, peel it and crush two parts for the two temples, then make an incision in the forehead where the pain lies so that you can place the crushed aloes under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is placed there, tie it up tightly and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then untie it and draw out the pennyworth of garlic, and let the wound remain thus for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on top until it protrudes from the wound.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the dressing has healed completely;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see that, then perform some of the cauterizing medicines I have written about or treat with cauterizing medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery follows this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called 'closed' because the head is shaped like a clove with a depression in the middle and a small opening in the midst;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, then hold your hand and twist the fire lightly until half of the point of the heart-shaped blade is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is behind, and let abundant blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterward, apply cotton wool soaked in oil and leave it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply cotton moistened in wax, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is clean.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', do so at its entire tip, being careful not to touch the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	de migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine as we have mentioned earlier in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterization previously described in medicine does not help, then you must heat the cautery called "culterellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And take thus on the pulsating place a line half the length of two fingers, and lift your hand once, ensuring that you do not touch the artery and that you do not go as far as the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the jawbone that moves when chewing, and let the nerve have no regard for its movement so that spasms do not come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting may cause great fear, especially to one who is not skilled and experienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And leave the wound open in mid-air;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it is appropriate in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the illness, and the patient endures pain, cauterize him by the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cautery having two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And these cauteries are better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Here is the French text for "of the pain of the ears due to cold":
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes to the ear and one has opened medicinal solutions thereupon and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pointe"
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After, prick all around the painful ear, or around both if the pain holds in both, and mark the spot a little away from the root of the ear where you will start.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make ten pricks around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat it until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the Torture of the Mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Only torticollis that moves from fluid should be cured by cautery;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not perform cauteries on those similar ones that come from heat and inflammation of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this kind of affliction that moves due to the flow of water and cleansings of the head and gargling, if it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third between the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery mark above the head of the ear somewhat below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger joint;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery until half of the brand is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And that is the shape of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And this type of cauterizing knife is similar to what we have shown before, but it is slightly more delicate and the blade should be a bit thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the place as I said before, make sure it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	If you have an ancient case of apoplexy which you treat as we have said and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries on them.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two cauteries on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one where it is called "vessels," as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And they should be treated as we have said previously.
de litargie	Of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large drinks and pills that cleanse the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	Then raise the patient's head up completely, and place on their occiput the plaster of mustard that is written about in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the method for cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he becomes better in this way, then it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if he does not improve, make three cauteries on the middle of the head going down to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And treat it as you would others; if you see him sweat, then apply the cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if necessary, apply two more on either side of the first two, and continue treating until healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And let the cautery used be called 'olivare', as I have mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hairs and of those things which we have mentioned before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After raising the patient's head, then apply the cautery to the top of the head, on each horn, and one behind and three along the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, then apply four cauteries along the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let him remain until the strongest heat has passed, then raise your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	Then treat until healed, using the cautery called 'olivare', which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The person suffering from epilepsy should not use a fire cautery unless they are phlegmatic. It is necessary to first modify the brain with remedies and other treatments that we have mentioned in the previous division, especially when the patient is large and tolerant of difficult medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, have them gargle and chew soft foods frequently to cleanse the brain.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	Then place the king's head in the middle, and perform the cautery as we have mentioned before, and cauterize the vessel and each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and enduring, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and weakness of body, on the spine of the back and neck, using olive oil according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When excesses or corrupt humors are present due to melancholy, then apply the cautery of many cauteries as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the excess is inclining towards melancholy due to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is mentioned beforehand in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	Then place the patient's head.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Next, make a linen bandage, also like a circle, and put it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And let the patient sit cross-legged, and be held firmly on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Next, present the lint, and melted old sheep's butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	Heat it over a moderate fire until the dough can withstand having the hot water poured onto it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After emptying the circle from within around the head, let it cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to the patient once each week with another good regimen until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	But if you want to cauterize it, make several punctures all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain excessively;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then place moistened cotton in butter and chicken fat upon it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin by giving the patient something to drink that cleanses the head and guards against all moistures, and make them sweat or take several baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After the patient reclines their head back, perform a cautery on the head and make two cauteries on both temples if the descent of the eye is affected at both eyes together, or one cautery on the temple where the descent occurs.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And cut all veins and arteries that are below the heart beneath each cautery, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of loss of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	I will teach you how to extract arteries and make an incision with caution how you should extend them;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And sometimes a cautery or hot iron is applied beneath the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are chronic and accustomed and lie upon the veins or near the arteries that appear on the forehead.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that they are cold surplus of phlegm, then he performs the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of the forehead descending towards the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I perform one cautery in the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hot irons beneath the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if there is need for more, then he cauterizes the eyebrow bloodily above each small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat according to what we have said in this division and it does not help at all, then give the patient three nightshade apples to drink.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king's head, he performs a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And perform two cauteries called 'clavilis' on the two shins, a little below the knees;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	And beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivary.
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the shape
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, perform two cauteries on the two shins as long as the hairs are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand there except until about a third of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have spoken of.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelashes turn inward and prick the eye; in this case cauteries are performed in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	That is to say, by fire, or by burning medication.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in your hand;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After tracing on paper the shape of an eye that resembles the opening of a mussel shell; let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then place damp cotton in egg white and powdered rose leaves on the eye; then heat the cautery whose shape is as follows:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Then cauterize along the figure you have traced, little by little many times, until the skin is burned at that spot.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of the work's health is that you see the paper retreat and the hairs stand upright at the tip of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, leave it like this for three days; then place damp cotton in butter until the burn is healed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply ointment until it is sound.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs grow back and the paper becomes softened, then begin the cautery again on that same spot, just as you did at first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If the hairs are missing, cauterize until the skin lifts back to its natural level and becomes even, without pricking the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of fire used in medicine should be ordered to the patient so that they let their hairs grow long and even, then make a shape like the leaf of a myrtle from parchment.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take one dram each of French soap and live chalk, grind them together thoroughly.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf and place it over the paper covering the eyes.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	If the patient has disease in one eye only, work on that one; if both eyes are affected, do so for both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And place moistened cotton under the eye with a sparrow's egg.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	Hold the patient's head steady in your hand and place your two fingers over the medicine, pressing gently on it each time the patient feels the heat of the medicine, as they will feel heat like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the cauterization is over, then lift up the wound, and check if you see the paper raised as it would be by the constraint of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply more medication to the wound where the medication has not opened until your work is even, and your eyes are on target;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place cotton soaked in butter over it until the heart's heat subsides, afterward cleanse the wound with ointment called 'diaphoresis' and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must take great care in your work, lest any medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes moist afterward, and the hairs prick at the eye, then recommence the medication on that wound which has softened from the proper paper, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cleanse it until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of cauterizing with a hot iron:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this let your constraint be.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the straight path be closed off to him who practices this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	The translation of "de la cure de fistule par cautere" is:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then you must perform a cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head on your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And take the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or turn its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then place cotton moistened with egg white or onion juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	Then heat the cautery that is thus shaped:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and is shaped like the top of a dove's feather, with the cautery being level together;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you see it, let one end be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see it, let it also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this which is shaped is more useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Then press the fistula if it is open, and remove the corruption and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, then open it, and draw forth the bowels.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Then place the hot cautery firmly upon it, and keep your hand on the cautery at the part of the eyelid above the eye, so that your hand does not act foolishly.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And place the cautery in the fat around the eye, and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone at the beginning of the cautery, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and again if necessary, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After that, put on gauze moistened in butter, and continue the drying ointment until it is healed. And if after forty days it has not healed, then apply a caustic medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And follow the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is also a method of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand this: fistulas, cut them open;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Then insert into the opening one small tube made of this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	And they do it to the amount of one-third of a pound;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand firmly over the cauterizing tool, and let the patient not move his head at all, so that the molten lead does not spill onto his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and one must put on the patient's eye moistened cotton dipped in egg whites or egg yolk:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead is then placed at the location of the fistula, and healing occurs miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	**And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have spoken of, that is good.**
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	**If not, then it is necessary to administer a probe to the nose and bring the fistula back to its proper place in the body of the nose.**
des crevaices en levres	"cracks in lips"
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	"Often, cracks in the lips called 'splits' occur, especially on children's lips."
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	"If you treat these cracks according to what we have said in divisions and the treatment does not work, then heat a small cautery knife according to this shape:"
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And quickly place it in those crevices until it reaches the source;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply cerate to the location until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	"of the boil on the throat"
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat, in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes decay and rot, becomes inflamed, and turns into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said through incisions, but it does not help:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must apply cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the blow or puncture of the fistula, keep your hand there until the hot iron reaches its base, and behind it;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this once or twice, after the treatment we have described in our cures, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if it is cured thus, that is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	But if not, then uncover the spot and remove the rotten bone according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	"of the movement of teeth"
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't help, then put the patient's head in your lap.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After heating the cautery whose shape will be described below, so that you place a band around the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And quickly put the hot cautery inside and keep your hand there until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	Then lift your hand and resume the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After, the patient fills their mouth with salted water, holds it for an hour, and expels rich fire.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	"And in this way the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum is strengthened, and the corrupt moisture dries up."
de la dolor des dens	"of toothache"
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from coldness, where there is coldness or wind, and the treatments of medicine do not help, then there is need for a cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, put the tip into an iron or brass spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a needle, dip it in melted butter, quickly place it on the painful tooth, and hold until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. Then if you see that wrapping wool and cotton in cold butter and placing it on the aching tooth helps, heat iron until fire comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauteries made of fire are such that you should take one made of iron or brass, and it should be so thick that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, which will be described later, place it on the tooth and keep your hand there until the cautery is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then rinse well;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever size you desire, and according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the shape of the tin can:
des scrophules	"Regarding scrofula"
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrophules are caused by phlegm and cold moistures and are not responsive to digestion through medicines, then heat the hair cautery, of which the shape is given below, and let it have two openings for the smoke to exit from the other end;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice until it reaches the base of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	If the abscess is small, apply a cautery according to its size, and leave it on for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And apply moistened cotton in butter until the burn is healed.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails in the pores of the lungs, especially when it is due to a cold temperament, then the patient must first be evacuated by soluble medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Then apply a cautery at the root of the throat, ensuring not to go all the way up to the throat and not to burn deeply but only slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Then apply another cautery at the junction of the neck and head of the spine, using the cautery called "clavicle," as shown above.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the area until it is healed, as previously mentioned.
de la toust	"of cough"
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all diseases of the lungs are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or cough, and if it is an old disease, apply two fire cauteries on the chest in empty places.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And one cautery between the breasts near the nipples
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery called "clavile" be made according to the shape described earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see fit, apply a cautery prick at every point where the cautery called "pointe" is used, whose shape is depicted above in diseases of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let there be up to thirty points, or as many as needed around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterward treat the area according to what is said earlier, and use a cautery with three rows according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	"And because cauteries are lighter by making three at once."
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	"of the dislocation of the auxiliary ligament"
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterward, make the patient lie on their back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then raise the heart which is inside the armpit with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inward, heat the cautery that has two branches until it resembles this shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the lung until it pierces through to the side, and the figure of the cautery should resemble four cauteries combined.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	And therefore cauterization is done with a cautery having three heads, because the marks of cauterization are six.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are as fine as a thread, and that is the shape of the cautery with three heads:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is added onto this 1 nerve, therefore there are 8 cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterwards place on the cautery powdered wormwood with salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until they are well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upward, which happens rarely, then perform a cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavile, or many pricks with the cautery.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For once the joint is closed and the moisture removed, the patient will be healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and excessive moisture accumulate in the stomach, altering its complexion and increasing phlegm despite customary treatments showing no benefit, then the patient should lie on their back, extend their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then perform three cauteries: one beneath the elbow of the arm equal to two fingers, entirely covering the clavicle, and two cauteries on either side of the ribs so that the marks of the cauteries form three angles, with enough space between each other so they do not join together when they throw out corruption.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the cauteries be deep enough to reach both parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see someone cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and holding it on the stomach for one point according to the amount you see fit;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with all of the cautery that is called 'point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment described above, ensure it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, so much that it is far removed from its natural composition due to excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, but it does not help him, then the patient must be made to vomit.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and apply three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the rib cage comes.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	And keep a space of two fingers between each cautery;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long in length and do not press your hand too much on all of the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And let only half of the heart burn, and let the patient lie on his right side.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot do this, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms.
et c’est li forme:	This is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and ensure that you do not burn all the heart, for you would cause the whole body to dry up.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And let it not come near the belly, for the heart is very delicate there, and the flesh also.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strong.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, he feels madness-making pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then, when this treatment is applied by physicians, the patient must be made to sweat on his head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then, press firmly on the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that resembles a ray. Here is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the flesh is burned and come to siphon, so that all pus flows out.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After treating according to the treatment of abscesses until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And only those who have studied medicine for a long time and by whom many such illnesses have been cured should use this cautery.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can daringly operate; nevertheless it seems to me that it is better for him to leave (it).
dou cautere de pleuresin	Regarding the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy with roots of bistort, in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a large, dry root of bistort, as thick and long as your two fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	And boil it in oil, then take it to the fire and make one large cautery between the shoulder blade and neck, and two smaller ones a little way down towards the area under the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And place two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly backward.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And one cautery in the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on both sides of the breast below the cautery between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	Do not press your hand, but hold it open as in smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancient authorities say that certain men used to employ a fire cautery resembling that of a barber, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reached the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And when there is pain outside, as we have said concerning the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	Yet in this operation there is fear, for the patient may die now, or a fistula may occur which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Regarding mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice according to what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not help at all, then there are 3 good ways of cautery that can be used:
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	One method is to make three or four cauteries in a line according to the length of the mouse's body, following the shape of the liver cautery that we have described earlier.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	And do not press your hand during the entire cautery process, and let the patient lie constantly on their back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	And another method of cautery is to heat the cautery that has two edges, as we have shown in the case of shoulder dislocation;
