et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be as long as two finger widths across the forehead downwards until it reaches the nose, and the other two should be at either side above the eyelids, but beware of cutting the arteries that are situated on both sides above the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And keep your hand away from the line of the lower jaw, let each cut be the size of three barley grains across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And prepare a sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then insert the spatula two parts of which are shaped like this:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the first cut that is due down the temple to the second cut;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Then peel away all the skin that is between the two incisions up to the eyebrow bone above the eye, then do similarly from the middle cut to the other second cut, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision an instrument called a "cautery knife", which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other without being sharp; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of the blade towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and press until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut away all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where the heart opens, then similarly do in the middle cut down to the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	then drain the blood evenly, and press the site for the collected blood.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put a bandage of old cotton in each incision, and cover them with cloths moistened in wine, oil, and axle-grease, ensuring that no abscesses form.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	On the third day, loosen the bandages and apply abundant cold water compresses; then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the remedy for headaches
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	If the veins come with Cataract accustomed to appear, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weaken sight, and burnt papers;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	And hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head with fever, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore know by these symptoms that those materials and that catarrh come only from many veins, and the cure for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should command the patient to raise their forehead, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another from ear to ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, going down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves near the temples that move while chewing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge; then open between the two lips of the wound and place cotton wool and linen strips.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then, tie wet cloths moistened in wine and oil upon it, and guard against hot abscesses.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When the bone is removed, then you must rub it until flesh begins to grow, and then treat it with drying agents that promote tissue growth.
En teil maniere:	In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And apply it to these wounds to promote tissue growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter on the Stopping of Ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of four things
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or some kind of creature, or a piece of metal ore or similar thing like iron
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as water and eye mucus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When something like a stone or another object falls into the ear and does not fit or grow in it, place the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then pour some drops of violet oil or sesame oil onto it, and then perform extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And when it sneezes, cover its nostrils with a cloth or wool wick when the sneeze comes, and place around the ear
et estent l’oreille au desus.	And they lift up the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often fever comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if fever does not come, he should perform extraction with fine forceps; here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it bursts open with the forceps, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then perform extraction using a thin hook of small thickness;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not come out with that, then make a reed of thin bronze and insert the tip of the reed into the hole in the ear with force, and plug what is around the reed with soft wax so that the vein cannot enter with the reed;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then draw out the fever strongly, for often fever comes as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come out in this way, then take some pitch like what is used for birds, and put some on an instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put some cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the pitch onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw out the fever.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out of all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before a hot abscess arrives and causes spasm;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient lie on their back, and draw out blood according to his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear at the level of the fat.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then break it according to your strength and suck it out quickly with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And continue treating him until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's a stone that is inside and it is inflamed, then perform an extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it cannot come out, then administer the thin, subtle spatumile in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And arrange incising of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this if you think that the stone is moist due to the moisture of the ear until you have broken it into many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract with subtle tweezers and sugar, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, when water falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to perform sneezing several times and fill the ear with old cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many needles according to the length of your middle finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	And let the patient insert one or more of these needles into his ear, and stick out on the other side with its foot, then pierce another needle onto the one that is in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	And do not stop piercing needle into needle until all the water flows out, and thus it will all flow out.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see, then take a reed, insert one end into the ear and wrap the other end in fire until the reed is well burnt.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then repeat with other reeds until all the water flows out, as we have said earlier about needles.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In extracting an insect, if it is small bodied, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the section on dissection.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it's from a large body where one can feel it, then introduce the extraction of forceps.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the easiest thing to remove that exists in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In extracting worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in division and where treating distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must examine the ear in sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If no worms appear, use fine forceps to remove them, and if none are seen, then take the tube with the form as follows:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert its finest tip into the ear according to the amount of suffering experienced by the patient, then suck strongly through the entire tube;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, then stuff cotton around the tube as I have said regarding stones;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they still do not come out as we have said, then introduce the distillations that the ancients have proven effective in killing worms, and you will find them discussed under treatments for distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And then drip your oils and medicines into the ear with all this equipment, of which there is the shape here as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be made of silver or thin brass underneath with small holes, and above for dripping.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And for pressing inside the distillation, have an instrument made of well-made brass for this purpose, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip carefully;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then pour your oil or juice, along with what you wish of your medicines, into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then insert the razor with all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil has distilled out of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient sense it inside, and let the distillation be a warmed flask over the fire before you drip it into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Ensure that it is not too cold, for then the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter on the Stopping of Ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without any holes in their ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And the same is true for adults through injury to the ear, or flesh growing inside it, and these blockages sometimes occur deeply within the ear so that they cannot be seen.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Sometimes there is a defect in the hole and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Therefore, when one occurs deeply and cannot be seen, it is difficult to treat in many cases, and in the case where it can be seen, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun.
et regarde dedens:	And look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the obstruction apparent, then proceed according to the method described here.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	Let it be pointed and sharp in front and behind, so that it does not cut into the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the obstruction is flesh growing or a growth in the ear itself, then use fine forceps to gently pluck it out until all of that flesh has been removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wax is deeply embedded in the ear, take a fine, light razor and heat it slightly over fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you notice the operation from which the patient feels pain upon hearing it, pierce easily, and ensure that you do not harm the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then place in the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moist it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a wick and moist it with rose water, then sprinkle ground glass powder upon it;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swelling up, then it is necessary to remove the wick and insert another one moistened in cerote which has been made with rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then continue treating it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is discharge of blood, take a sponge and wrap it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	That is to say, "of the flesh of the papers"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These growths that come on paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry should be stretched out with forceps and pincers, and cut off with a spathula at their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then place ground glass powder upon the wound.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if there is blood on the skin, then cauterize it with a small round cautery; after the incision, movement will be easier.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often they return, for nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often there come upon the eyes things like hail in shape and hardness, and therefore this illness is called 'hail'; it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The operations are as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Be aware if the 'hail' moves from side to side; this is easy to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make an incision of moderate size, gently scrape off each part, then grasp it with forceps and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot remove it without piercing the paper a little, do not worry about harming the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the wound is large, join it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not apply too much force, for the ointments will heal it soon and join flesh together.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if hailstones fall inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, grasp the hailstones with tweezers, and cut and press them from one side to the other.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the paper moves away due to the incision, it matters not.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And once the hailstones are cut out, rinse the ear with saltwater, and treat the place where flesh joins until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Euxinach is a grease that enters the threads of paper wicks and this happens more in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes. In the mornings, they have cataracts and cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And for this reason they lie on their faces constantly, and sleep thus, with their papers beneath their wet eyelashes so that the inflammation and appearance cover the exinatch which opens into the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press hard with your thumbs and feel the exit through them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of working is such that the patient places their head in your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	Then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinatch from each part, then place it on top;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	And press with your two thumbs on either side so that the exinach is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then make in the middle of the moisture with the sharp spatula a slit no wider than the wound made when letting blood;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	And cut through the skin so deep that you reach the exinach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in many cases exinach comes out of the slit like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract then a whole piece of soft cloth between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to left and right until it is dispersed;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and ensure you do not touch the opening with your fingers lest you reach all the way to the eyeball and accidentally cut yourself.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exit wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, gently widen it a little until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract as we have said, then wet cloths in warm water and put them on the wound, and bandage it tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who crush bile and place it on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the burn until it is clean.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to its head, then cauterize it with gentle emplasters until it is clean.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of the skin
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural to them and are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases such as constant tearing and softening of the lids and cloudiness, leading to damage to the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And there are four ways to treat it:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Either by burning cautery together with fire, or by hot medicine as described earlier in the chapter on cauteries, and it is done either by incising and stitching or by tweezers, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is inverted, that's good
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, then insert a needle along all the threads
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let this be near the edge of the paper where the hairs grow around these hairs, and draw the thread upwards along all the paper, and turn it towards the razor
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part below the paper, below the hairs close by, with all the scalpels fitting, from the large ear down to the small
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then press on the paper with an iron, like a minting hammer, but be sure that the figure matches the quantity you see lifting up the paper that is divided into twelve parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if one needs to cut off a large amount of the paper according to how soft it has become
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then draw on all the spleen according to the two lines you have marked out, beginning from the large kidney stone up to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then place the cautery into one of the two corners of the heart, and burn it completely;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then join the two lips with a single stitch of an awl and fine thread; wipe away the blood, and wipe off any gluey substances on the eyebrows if you see fit to do so.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, pay it no mind; then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then heal the wound without stitches using dry and constricting substances; for paper adheres to the union of the wound and impedes it, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients say); this is done without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And there is another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And it is that you draw on the paper a figure similar to the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three points spread out according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut those which are above the small squares evenly according to the form which is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you lack the power to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread attached and insert it into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and place one thread near the large tear, and the second thread near the small one, and bring together the threads evenly between your two fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift up all the skin where you have marked it, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar softening ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And sometimes the hairs of the paper are curled.
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	Thus you must use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But stitching in one way or another is more artistic.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of cankers is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you fold the paper and pierce it according to what I have said, and then make two cankers by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut off two heads of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then join the two subtly on what is above the paper of the eye, and press the two cankers of the two parts firmly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for a few days, and the skin that is pressed will die and blacken and peel off until it falls away by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, cut it with some force, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is closed and the paper lifted, hairs will no longer grow there;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two splints you shall make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The procedure is as follows: take a fine needle, and thread through it one strand of soft silk.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then tie the heads together gently, with the length of the threads being a palm's length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then take another fine silk thread briefly, and tie its ends together.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then have the patient place their head in your hand;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And stand in the sunlight so that the procedure is clearly visible; for it is a subtle and delicate procedure. Then insert the needle along the entire length at the root of the hair, pressing into the paper quickly until you draw it out naturally along the hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull the hair out until it reaches the needle's eye, and insert into the eye one or two or three hairs or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then draw your hand across until the hairs come out entirely on the paper with their natural growth.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the hair is plucked and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the hair at the bottom until all the threads that you have ordered are gone, so that the hair comes out entirely from the hole above and you can see it with your eyes.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then pluck out the hair and thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hair grows back in its place and flesh forms on top.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are short, then accompany them with one long hair from the head, and lift it up with that one which you leave until it is lengthened and then raise it up.
de la porriture de l’oil	About the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes to the eye, there are two ways to treat it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One is natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, or from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the operation is that you cut this joint, separate its lips, and place linen tents within it, until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and thou shouldst not use in the treatment thereof things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if thou dost this, then returns the illness worse than it was before.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but there ought to be applied things softening, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and rosewater or saltwater and linseed boiled, and applications of diaculion melted in some oil, and it should be wrapped with a linen cloth, and the treatment thereof.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the aim of thy treatment is that thou shouldst take care that it does not heal according to its former shape.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these operations which we have spoken of are but redressings of this disease, that it may not return according to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	About flesh growing in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is below what is truly called "axacrati" is natural and accidental
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and cut and burn and things similar;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way to perform this operation is that you take a needle with a doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left eyelid towards the right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then stretch the flesh above the entire needle and cut it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	But if not, then take a razor and place it in the crease, turn the paper over, and make two cuts inside the paper along its edges.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the ends of the two cuts be the two corners of the incision you have made, and form an angle such that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of the Greek letter 'I'.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that piece of flesh according to the length and width of its edges from under the paper, then join together the two parted sides and sew them with a thread of wool.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the care of those we have spoken about regarding mollifying medicines, and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a split or cut or burn, then you should make a full-length split under the pubic hairs, following what is written above;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then insert between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one should perform the procedure according to the shape of the disease, for it is very varied in shape; and wise masters arrange all their strength to make the form return to its natural state
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the procedure and tools in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	About the sudden tearing of the paper (i.e., the eyelid)
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this union happens in many men in such a way that the skin above is stuck with the white of an egg and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should put the point of a razor under the skin and lift it up
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And stretch them like tweezers, until you grasp what is suitable for the subtile spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer if the spatula is too sharp or blinds the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And make your cut, from which you scrape away that collection, lightly so that the paper returns according to its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And remove all of that collection, and sometimes apply salted water to the eye, then rinse with fresh water and collyrium;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place a linen tampon between the paper and the eye, and apply wool moistened in egg albumen onto the eye;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after the third day, apply cold compresses until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that a nail can be in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	Either it is nervous and similar to hard skin, or another that is not nervous but resembles moist gel, which when touched by iron and attempted to be grasped with tweezers, cannot be held.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both kinds begin near the great eyelid, growing gradually until they cover all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	Then the manner of incision is such that the patient places his head in your hand, then opens his eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	And lift the paper to your hand, then fold the corner like small tongs, and press it on top;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	And fold the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the corner, pushing it through completely with the needle, then tie the corner with thread and press it down, and scrape off all the hair on the side of the corner that covers the pupil and silk to the top of the hair, then cut the remaining at the root of the eyelid with a sharp scalpel and tweezers, leaving the natural flesh on the eyelid so that tears do not flow through the incision as usual;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes the nail grows only on the little finger, and on the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then remove all the soft skin around this area; here is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And ensure that the spatula does not touch and tear the delicate tissue, and that the needle is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	After the incision, pour some crushed celery seed into the wound, and make a plaster of litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat this condition until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not painful and you cannot insert the needle, nor can tweezers enter, often this type of nail is cured by medications;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I have described in the section above; if you observe them carefully, open the wound of the patient and gently take a little spatula according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And carefully raise the nail up; and if you see that it does not thin out and the root is pressed, then distill from your mouth into the wound a plaster made of litharge and red lead and crushed celery seed, and seal the wound until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then continue the other operation according to this same work until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing stands in your way with the eye, such as a hot abscess, then apply the cautery, first treating the hot abscess until it is clean, then resume the work as before until it is clean.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid causes harm to the eye with great damage, then suspend it with a needle and cut off a part, but not all, so that no tears come from it.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men's eyes, there sometimes grows red flesh which covers the pupil and sticks to the membranes, pushing them forward like a pomegranate seed.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the operation is this: the patient places his head in your hand, then you open his eyes and grasp all that red flesh with suitable hooks, and hold it firmly
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut off the first piece of flesh, and keep cutting until it is all removed, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And the incision of the eyelid should be made in the same way as the incision of the nail and the small ligaments from which bone is removed, as shown later in this chapter
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply to the eye crushed celery seeds or distill upon it red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines; then place on top a wisp of cotton with egg white so that it may be securely sealed against a hot abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	And if anything remains and the wound begins to grow hot, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave off the eye treatment and cure the abscess with cool remedies.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your original task once it is healed, and thus do in any case where flesh has adhered to the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless you should relieve the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural course;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	And also according to any accidental course, in regard to iron work.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Do not put your hand into any of these operations while you see that this limb is suffering from such treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before veins are red which cover over the eye, causing their operation to be obscured and weakening the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary for you to first examine whether the eye, in which there is an abscess, is hot and if there is no other feverish illness besides the abscess;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Then tie it in such a way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Command the patient to place his head on your knee, then suspend those veins according to their wisdom, and let the bandages be doubled subtly according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two onions per degree in a single course according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then tie the bandages tightly, pressing gently on the veins, and squeeze out blood drop by drop until you see the veins swell beneath the skin.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And be sure not to cut the eye with the points of the tweezers, and perform this procedure at midday before the sun, being very diligent in your work so that you do not let any blood flow other than from those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, then distill into the eye a mixture of green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the stone.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot remove the stone completely in one sitting, then apply a plaster made of soothing substances to the eye until the pain is eased and an abscess forms. Then resume according to this method until the patient is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	And these are the forms of remedies:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	A surgeon calls a fistula 'arissati':
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with a cautery and with medicine that burns hotly according to what I have said before, and it is not yet healed, then there is deceit within it which you should cut upon the abscess where it must be burst, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then cut with all the instruments that are mentioned here in their proper form:
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And this is called 'sharp head', and should be made of hot iron from its head to its end, and be pointed like a chisel as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the location of the rotted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is scraped.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And do this several times, then apply medicinal remedies that dry up (the wound).
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the place is sound and flesh is born there, and the body of the bow is sound, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew nor become inflamed, and no evil happens to it, know that it is healthy.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nostril according to this method:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And it is that you uncover the bone with iron a second time, and with hot medicines; and when it is uncovered take iron forceps in this shape, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and thin out the handle up to its end as shown here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye socket; then turn the forceps entirely until it pierces the bone, which the patient will feel because the wind will hiss if they hold their hand over their nostril
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you; and when the flesh has grown and the joints have hardened, then it will go to snow.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	So it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When both eyes open fully and evenly, and nothing obstructs or diminishes them, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heat [the patient], then place cupping glasses or leeches without cutting to suck; then put on the eye a poultice made of aloe and frankincense and sarcocolle, and then close the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloth.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one into four layers, then place them one on top of another according to how much the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then secure it tightly with a hard bandage from above and then recommence the cupping glasses to suck without cutting;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye constrained day and night. If the ligature loosens, then you must pull it out.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the ligature after the day and night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good.
se ce non;	If not,
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then resume the emplastrum and dressings and ligature and cupping glasses until it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a burst eyeball
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	If disruption comes to the eyeball wound, then it opens, and blood flows from the paper like a grain of resin, which is frightening to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it close, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then insert another needle where there is the doubled thread of the eyelid.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it with this, leaving the first needle in its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then tie the doubled thread at a suitable location and bind one part of the eyeball around it tightly. Then remove the needle and place a damp linen cloth soaked in egg white over the eye.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Allow it until the thread falls out with the boil, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And sometimes the wound is held closed by the boil on each side of a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye appears swollen, then pierce it with a fine needle that comes from deep within the eye, and draws out the moist albuginous humor and causes the eye to descend, entering therein quickly.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyelid
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This condition called 'alcunnati' is nothing but bowed moisture assembled in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	To observe the appearance of this condition, make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the bowing rise up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then it should be inserted, without descending, and the light should be removed; let the patient see as he used to.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the bowel is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and pierce through the corneal tissue one or two fingers along the length of the conjunctiva with the cornea and crown until the bowel exits.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And once it has exited, distill hot water mixed with honey or boil fennel seeds in water and honey, then cleanse it with another dressing until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Aigues of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have shown the similitudes of acute conditions in the division, and those that should be pierced;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if you work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and tightly bind the sound eye.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if it is right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if the eye is right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument near the crown where it is about the thickness of a ray on the eyelid at the side closest to the lesser eyelash, then gently push the instrument called 'almagda', turning your hand until it pierces into the eyelid and you feel that almagda reaches the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And ensure that the measurement of the path of 'almagda' is equal to the length from the measurement of the space between the pupil and the end of the blackness.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone through this paper due to the clarity of the corneal cloth, then place the instrument up to where the water is, and then express it along one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If water descends now, then the patient sees before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a moment, if the water rises up the second vein, then apply pressure with the instrument; and when it is inserted deeply and it does not rise, then gently extract the almagda while rotating your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	Then put back in water a drop of this precious stone, and rinse out the eye with it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place a plug made of wool soaked in rose oil and egg yolk over the eye, securing it with healthy eye ointment.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we put crushed cumin on wounds with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then carefully pierce only the conjunctiva, not too deeply but rather gently and delicately; insert the almagda as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And when the operation is complete, prepare a comfortable resting place for the patient on his back in a dark room.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And keep him still from all movements; let him eat light foods and not move his head either to the right or left, and have him bound according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then he unties him in that same dark house, and tests his sight, and makes him see some things, and then puts the bandage back on for seven days.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	but you must not do this during the hour of treatment or after incision immediately, but you should lay him down, because water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess begins to form, untie the bandage before the seventh day, and apply a poultice that alleviates abscesses
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is soothed, then uncover the sight and put on his face a piece of linen to cover for a few days, and keep him always in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then gradually leave the house little by little, and let him gradually return to his usual way of life.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciples should interfere in this case
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And someone came to us from Iraq who said that in some lands they make an instrument called almagda for piercing the eye, through which water is sucked out, but still I have never seen one in our land nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it may be a new thing
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of Almagest forms, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be made of pure silver
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And their fronts should have this same subtlety, and their backs should have three sharp angles."
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes joints grow together unevenly, among which some resemble scorptions with many feet
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And there are such that have flesh of yellowish color, and soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	Therefore, in those soft flesh which is not hard, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and pour oil on that flesh, and rub it forcefully.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	for cut away everything that you can sustain with a sharp knife from one side until you know that all the flesh is removed
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut away, then open it with all the delicate instruments lightly, so that nothing remains
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	And if blood overflows, or a boil breaks open, then cleanse it promptly as is necessary.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if they are malignant boils, then hurry and cauterize them until the blood is staunched and all the flesh is removed, then apply fresh lint and wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If new growth occurs, and moisture reaches the mouth, know that it is without disease;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if moisture does not permeate as it should, know that there is bone growing above the flesh, to which the instruments do not come for cutting:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Therefore you must insert a thick linen thread into it, moistened with our hands, and have between each knot at least one finger or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And let the patient put his head on the thread's end with some force, and pull it out while smelling until it comes into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	And many children do this at school, and it is easy for those who wish to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then grasp the head that comes through the snow with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart gently, as we do who are present.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the wound has corrupted that flesh, then pull out the threads, squeeze out the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian oil, and replace it into the snow as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of the flesh
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then place in the snow a hot poultice for some days until it is healed, and if dry medicines are needed, use them
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, in which one distills oils and medicines onto the snow
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a tube, with its channel also
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the head
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let him have much of this to hold his head when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Frequently, a disease called 'telul' appears on the head and grows large, becoming visible to see.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason, you must cut it off at the beginning, and then remove all the skin, before applying a cautery or hot medicine.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	And if one delays cutting until it is large, then beware if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted abscess; for when it is cut, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess is soft to touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then empty the patient and cut without fear, and afterwards treat with drying and tightening things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and bleeding
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know this: when water comes into one of these joints, it does little good, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, one must examine whether the wound is entirely fresh in all its blood;
