et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then join the two lips to a stitch, then heal it until it is clean.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the lips are already dry on both sides, you must scrape away all parts of their core until they are sound, then join the two lips together with a stitch, and bind them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder, and crushed incense upon it.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the powders a strong plaster or other adherent plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is sound.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of stitching is that you bring together the edges:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the abdominal stitching.
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	lipomas
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	There are many people who have hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of millet, some smaller and others larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Therefore you must turn back the lips, make an incision on each knot, grasp it with forceps and cut it into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stanched.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the egg yolk, and heal the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often there appears on the joined gums a growth called "albulus" by the ancients;
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	Therefore you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, allowing the blood to flow freely.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then apply powdered vitriol or other restricting and drying powders to the wound;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	And if that flesh returns after being cut, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	These are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they appear gathered together at the head of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, rough and sharp excrescences;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and wormy, causing corruption in the gums, and the teeth stink.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and their shoulders be within your grasp, raising the teeth or the edges until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And likewise remove blackness, greenness, yellowness and other stains until they are clean;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one removes what is there due to the first cause, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then begin again on the second and third day until everything has been removed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that teeth require various forms of instruments to remove them according to what the task demands, for those used to remove protruding teeth have different shapes than those used to remove teeth between others.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	When curing a toothache, one must delay extracting as long as possible, for this should not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	For it is a very delicate structure until there is no excuse to extract.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained due to toothache, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and they believe it is from the tooth of St. Denis, and have their good tooth pulled out;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not leave because of this, so much that the bad one is removed, for we have already tried this with such sinners;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain about the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth all around with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Then move it with your two fingers or with fine forceps bit by bit until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the forceps;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And hold the patient's head between your knees, and keep it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these tools and insert it gently on each side, and with the lever, move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and hollowed out, then you must fill it with small wads of cloth where the hole is;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	And hold it gently with forceps so that it does not break when being pulled out.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	It is necessary to operate skillfully around the gum to extract a tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure that you do not break it, and if a piece remains, it will cause the patient greater pain from the root's wickedness than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that thou dost not do as foolish surgeons do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the cheekbone, and do not bring about what we have mentioned.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	But through their rashness they sometimes cause great diseases by the roots left behind or the cheekbone broken, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine, vinegar, and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the area
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	If that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shape of the tooth-extraction tools with which one first moves teeth should be long-pointed and thick-handled, so they do not bend when pulling the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	"And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend during extraction, and they should be made of good iron and have teeth to hold the tooth in place."
de la racine des dens	"for the root of the teeth"
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after extraction, you should place on the area cotton soaked in butter for one or two days until the area is softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri," with which the jaw resembles a parrot's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And they shall be made within as if with a file; this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root and insert into it the instrument called 'althali', which is like a spatula. And this is its shape:"
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by chance, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	But if not, then use all the tools whose forms are given hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	"And also help yourself with this instrument which has two rows, of which this is the shape:"
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	"and other iron instruments that are placed in front of the root of the teeth, and also help yourself with this instrument which resembles large pliers. And here is its shape:"
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this tool be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many tooth tools are like this;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	And also other tools which are not enumerated;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise master shall find his own tool according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where no ancient tools were taught due to their diversity; and if one breaks a carriage or other bones where it could be used, then one seeks among the tools that are necessary, which I have told you about, and uses gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can grasp and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore the joint with appropriate medications for this condition; if there is decay in the bone and it is small, scrape it away with all these tools.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When teeth appear not according to their natural course, and the form is ugly, especially in maiden women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is next after the one beside it and not in its proper place, and neither can be drawn nor smoothed.
adonques lou raie;	then remove it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is close to the tooth, take this tool whose shape is depicted here, resembling a small beak of iron sharpened on its end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	"And work little by little with your hands over several days to remove the tooth because of its hardness and so that you do not move the others. And if it is visible enough to be smoothed, then smooth it with a rasp like this one here, of which this is its shape:"
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and is also like the file used for making needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And gently file the tooth a little each day until it falls out without moving too much.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then smooth the edge at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it is necessary to file down its sharpness until it no longer hurts the tongue or impairs speech.
quant li dent lochent	"When teeth are loose:"
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth are knocked out, either by an impact or a fall, and the patient cannot chew their food without it falling apart, even after treating them with constricting medicines, then that is of no use;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then they should be secured with a gold wire, for silver becomes green and rotten, but gold does not change.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see that the teeth need to be straightened, then take the wire and the double-ended pliers between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or several, until you can barely see blood between the healthy tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start wrapping again up to where you began, and gently pull your hand tightly until it no longer moves.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the jaws of the file with some pliers, join them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, and position it so that it does not burn the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then let it remain thus tightly until it can stay, and if it loosens, or the files become round, tighten them with another file.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains thus, it will serve throughout its time, and this is the shape of teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, replace it in its place, gently, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And let no one who is not wise and patient meddle with this, and sometimes a tooth made from cow bone is used, placed in the space where there is a deficiency, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	"To cut the tie of the tongue:"
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this union comes naturally underneath the tongue at birth;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	In case of an accidental wound.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	And the treatment is as follows: open the patient's mouth, hold their head steady in your hand, and raise their tongue.
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Next, cut the frenulum of the tongue with a scalpel until the tongue is disconnected from its attachment. If there is scar tissue or a nodule present, which can occur due to an injury, insert the nail and cut it away.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	Ensure that the cut does not go too deep so as not to injure the artery located underneath.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	After performing this, lift up the jaw with warm rose water or warm vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen pad underneath the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And have the patient rinse their mouth each night so that the wound does not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	If bleeding occurs, place powdered vitriol on the wound.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	And if the blood flows abundantly, cauterize it with a slow-acting cautery that is suitable for this purpose.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then treat another wound until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see a fleshy growth of black or hard color which the patient cannot feel, do not touch it, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it tends towards blenching and there is moisture, then apply the onion poultice, make an incision with a sharp lancet, and release it on both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if blood hinders your work, then apply powdered vitriol until it is staunched, then return to your task until all bleeding stops.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then raise the area with stitches and needle, and treat other wounds until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	"throat abscesses"
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there are lumps that form in the throat which are called "godath," and these are properly known as tonsils. If you treat them according to what we have said previously but they do not heal, then be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a hard boil with little sensation and fleshy color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if they are red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron for fear of blood letting;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it is ripe, and then you shall sever it, where it will break on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of pale color round, and the root is slender, then have ready your instrument to cut, but first check if the boil is warmly resting and quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and their limbs in your hand, and they open their mouth and take the servant's breath between their hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, of which this is the form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it should be made of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with this instrument and see the boil, take the lancet and insert it into the navel, and draw it up more than you can bear;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take some things from the cloths with it, then cover it with the instrument, of which this is the form, that appears as force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And moreover, the heads are curved, and one towards the other, and are very sharp, made of iron or steel
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take pincers, of which here is the form:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be cutting on one side, and named on the other
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And after cutting one of the mandibles, cut the other in the same manner; then let the patient gargle with warm water and salt-water, and if blood flows, let the patient gargle with water or cooked pomegranate skins, or myrtle leaves, and similar things until the bleeding stops
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it until it is sound
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two mandibles; then cut them in the same way as the two mandibles are joined.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was close inside her throat, namely one of small size
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And indeed, I had nearly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if left thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that it filled both openings of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then quickly fetched a needle, inserted it into the woman's throat, and pierced through it with great force, cutting away a large portion of her windpipe.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I closed another part of the wound with the needle and opened her mouth, pressing down on her tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After this, I pierced these abscesses with the needle and cut away some of it; only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the woman's throat passage was opened, and she began to drink water then wine; I continued cutting away at this abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses kept returning, filling up again the space I had cleared out until it became very large once more.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I bandaged it and burned with the cautery within the throat
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left these parts, and I do not know what God did with him afterwards.
de l’uve	"de l’uve"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is inflamed and protuberant, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below, thick, and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the surrounding swelling is appeased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded together and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	if it is sanguine or of dark color or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to its manner of blennor and length, you should have the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the awl into the eye, draw it downwards, and cut with the first of two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of two testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut beyond what is naturally excessive;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, it hurts the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of two testicles, until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, then you must use an instrument for the cauterization to make him fearless.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp and burning.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	It is necessary that the patient put his head in your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with hot water so that it is neither too thick nor too thin;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and here is the shape of this instrument:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And at its top has a hollow where one puts the medicine, like the hollow of a spoon, and put the instrument over the whole eye with the medicine;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth away from the medicine inside, so it does not reach the throat.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour's worth of time until you see it turn black and the pain from the medicine has ceased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the eye socket until the cotton touches the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the cauterization with the medicine, then do so, and afterwards wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him rise from cold water, and let him rinse with gargarisms until he is clean.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This remedy is safer than incision or cauterization;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and mugwort and similar herbs, gather them all or some into one pot, put ashes there, and let it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pot should be well sealed with clay, and in the pot there should be an instrument for shaving like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be made of silver or brass, and one end put in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the canal until the eye is numbed;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards, repeat often until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot boil, for many things could happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not apply cauterization heat except during the draining of an abscess boil.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put the tip of an egg into it so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the eggshell does not let the steam harm the mouth, and this is a good combined remedy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often a bone, fish spine, or any other object becomes lodged in the throat.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So then you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue with the sunken instrument so that you may move the object.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you cannot see and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps then the object will be expelled through vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of apple, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And tie the sponge with thread, then stitch it together.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	When it reaches its place, she will stand up, and then you pull fire.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not come by fire from what we have said, then take the lead instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have its head raised high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	Be sure not to touch the epiglottis, lest the patient choke, nor push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And it is better for the patient themselves to insert the instrument, so that they know where the thing stands upright.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Then push it down until you draw fire evenly along the entire instrument, until it is fiery hot.
de la sansue de la gorge	**de la sansue de la gorge**
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the sinew is healed, as I said in my previous work, through treatment with medications;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And if this does not help, then observe the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after pressing their tongue with the instrument I mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see a vein, then tie it with a very small thread, or use fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not help, then take a peeled cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then place the end of the cane into hot iron and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats cold water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full handfuls of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the patient feels the water, they should lie down.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	If it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the same instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Repeat this many times, for it will fall without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	The manner of fumigation is thus: take a pot with live coals inside, cover the pot with a pierced cloth in the middle, and place the head of the instrument into that hole;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you throw your fumigation into it, and the patient places the head of the pipe in their mouth and closes their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but reaches the patient.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the boil will fall, and if it does not, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty foods also, but do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats sciatica is like this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps for entering into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it has the appearance of a bird's beak and sharpness like that of a rasp, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	Here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	"Chapter on Abscesses"
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses are described hereafter in this book, and they are differentiated by piercing and cutting.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And there are two types [of abscesses]: one is similar to itself, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the apostemes of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the apostemes of the fleshy part are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	But not all abscesses should be pierced until the boil has burst according to its fullness.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are some that must be pierced when they are ripe, even if they do not burst according to their fullness, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when apostemes come near joints, and one lets them be until they are completely rotten, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When an abscess is near the main limb, if you delay its opening until it becomes gangrenous, it will harm the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the fundament, pierce it before it becomes gangrenous
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without prior digestion being completed, except for one near the fundament, which might otherwise penetrate deeply and become an internal fistula
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and thus cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you should know the signs of opening a gangrenous abscess according to its development: when the pain stops, and fever subsides, and pain and redness decrease, and the swelling and hardness at the head of the abscess subside, along with other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the incision where the abscess hangs lowest and where it opens more easily
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the incision should be long enough for the body; and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints near arteries, make incisions equal in length wherever there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where they strike, follow according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better that you delay perforating until it is confirmed to be digested completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, then the body will be filled with its venom, and it is full of much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps it would harden the lips and the depth of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large holes, and many crevices according to the likeness of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to strike with fire and cauterize;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when they have become like thatches, and are softened, then you must do likewise as one does for boils.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that one cuts like the leaf of a mulberry tree, as abscesses of the angels;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like soft superficial abscesses, you must pierce them openly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when an abscess is large and it has collected much bowels, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bowels at that hour, but draw out one part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more afterwards;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly little by little until all the bowels come out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Similarly if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or very elderly men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because sometimes the spirit leaps with the release of the bowstring, causing the patient to die suddenly, without you noticing.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, proceed with great caution in this chapter, and once you have pierced your abscess, then cleanse the wound, and see if the wound from the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a deep incision, then bring linen or old cotton bandages;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it is a large abscess and there are many perforations, then you must stuff each one with a bandage so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut a piece of skin from the abscess, and you have shaved around it, then you must fill it with dry cotton or lint from linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the bandage, and apply an ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your operation, apply cold water and gauze, wet the cloth, and press it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book, especially during wintertime when the limbs or abscesses are very tense, then you should place hot wet cloths on them dipped in wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is summertime and the area is fleshy, then you must place wet cloths dipped in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then drain the abscess, clean it, and treat it until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this he must know universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	As I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, here is the chapter.
des soros	chapter on boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	**Where small boils come from the head**, they are like those we have in our skin, similar to the eggs of a goose, and there are many such similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture like mud;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and some that are hard and stony in appearance, and there should be no doubt if the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is that you test all tools called 'entromissoire', from which its form comes hereafter, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, so let it flow through above for a long time.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, scrape away without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns immediately if anything is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian oil if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, then in water and salt, and use it to dress the wound, leaving it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And this will consume what is remaining of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	Then recommence with cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know that none remains of the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the boil holds out fat, cut it according to this shape, along its length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cast your spices on it, and scrape it from all sides, and give all your care to draw out the clot that lies within it;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery opposes you, then do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do it for an abscess if it is hard, and with cutting and dressing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these boils have no moisture at their head, or are those boils that I cut from the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the boil just like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had struck it, they would have inflicted upon it as much of a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other boils coming at the head, besides those that come at the heads of children and the roots of ears, the incision should always be made in the lowest position so that the bowels may more easily issue forth.
et les cure si com il covient.	And treat him as it ought to be.
des scrophules	"Regarding scrofula"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck and under the armpits, and in angles, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and intermingled with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each boil is properly within its coat, like the pustule and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And there are many kinds of these boils.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also stubborn ones that refuse to heal.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	Among these, therefore, that which you see with good touch and is similar to the color of the skin, moves on each side and is not hard towards the nerves of the neck or the artery nor the vessel, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	Then you should cut it from above and scrape off each part; hold the two lips of the heart open if needed, as we have said for abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And cut it bit by bit, and make sure you do not cut the nerve nor the vein; let the scalpel be neither dull nor sharp so that your hand does not slip, nor go too deep lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not bleed freely, then place powdered vitriol or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and press the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is pacified, and the wound begins to soften and decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the bleeding has stopped, then return to your work, completing it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then search with your finger for any small scabs that may remain, cut them off and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	But if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, do not cut that scab at its root, but rather tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with Egyptian ointment-soaked cotton, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrophule, then it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them together now, since there is no longer any excess left due to the size of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must grasp the root of it and draw out fire, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	The scabs that hold excess fluid, prick where they open more.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it as before mentioned, depending on it, then bring plaster with ointment and similar things so that it may corrupt what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is clean, apply an ointment that penetrates deeply into the flesh until it is completely healed.
de squinance	Here is a possible translation of "de squinance" into English:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with squints, the flap of the throat called "epiglottis" must be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And one should not help by this means because all the veins and the membrane of the patient are hot in the mouth or throat or both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat of the lung, it is necessary to close the epiglottis to escape the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should do so below three circles or four, a small slit across between two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the thyroglossal duct, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are so connected to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh in them, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch out the skin of the neck at its full length, then cut the throat until it reaches the windpipe;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then cut the hyoid bone as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	This is demonstrated by the cutting of the windpipe's channel that leaps out from the place that has been broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a short time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed of which strangling is doubted, join together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it up entirely without cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the breath is gone.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient can swallow again and breathe through the wound, thus preventing death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore the ancients commanded that one should leave the wound open until the worst of the illness passes, and it passed in three days or four. And afterwards they commanded to sew up the wound and dress it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a damsel take a knife and stab it into her throat, and cut some of the veins of the lung.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	"I uncovered the wound and found that the blood issuing from it had not cut any vein nor carried off the throat, but the windpipe issued forth through the wound."
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed the wound, and dressed it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And nothing happened to the damsel except that her voice became hoarse, and later she returned to her usual self.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say do not fear cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	"of the large throat"
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This type of abscess is called 'throat hernia', and it is a large abscess with the color of a chestnut, occurring often in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	And there are two ways about this:
naturez, et accidens;	of essence and accident.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or it has no natural faculty.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accident is of two kinds: one resembles pus in some ways, and the other is like an abscess from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there should be fear in both cases, but one must only operate with fire when it is small, and prove and search this throughout the entire intromission.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like our pus and not attached to any vein, cut it off as we cut out pus; remove all of it if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Search everywhere around it, and treat it as needed until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	"of fatty tumors"
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of pus, all of which I will describe:
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must explain the difference between pus and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that discharge is hot and has fever as long as boiling does not pass, and corruption is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then, the fever and heat will cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without heat or fever or pain, the nut contains syrupac, which is its own juice and has the color of flesh. It starts like a jar and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And according to two similarities, it is either greasy or moist, with many colors as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When you come to the treatment of fatty tumors, first examine and explore with the instrument called the 'introitus', according to its form as described in the chapter that follows."
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of investigating boils is to take the moistest part you find in the boil and twist your fingers bit by bit until you know that the point has pierced the center, then continue according to the size of the boil.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the probe, taking care that nothing spills out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If there is running moisture in a boil of any color, cut it as I have said for other boils;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no moisture comes after the probe, know that it is greasy. Then cut it in a cross and take it with pincers, lightly scraping each side and carefully peel off the skin where it lies to draw it out cleanly with the nut.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	But if anything remains, the illness will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if even a bit remains, and the blood grieves you, then apply to the wound some hot caustic powders, bind the wound, and put on things that soothe an abscess heat, and treat with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the illness is great, then cut the two lips of the wound open, and treat those that go inward in flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the vein beating is against you or otherwise, then hasten and apply ground vitriol to its place, let it lie for two or three days until the wound rots, and let the blood ebullition rest;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to cutting those that remain of the boil.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the shapes of intrusive instruments, and they come in three kinds
grans et moien et petit;	Great, medium, and small
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are three squares called "albaret", one called "breb", and they come in three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Large, medium, and small to enclose the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles used to stitch wounds, and are made of yellow brass, iron, or silver; those that are gold are more valuable, and they are especially praised for enclosing the curves of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	And they come in three kinds
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Large, medium, and small according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the needles are very similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	And there are also needles with two curves that come in three kinds
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	And there are needles with three curves, which also come in three kinds
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	And there are needles with two curves and needles with one curve only, both of which come in three kinds
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these tools are sharp-edged, and there are some that cut only from one side, which are used to scrape off bone in order not to sever the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And among these introducers are the alemeles that are kept in many hands so that the patient does not perceive them during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	And they come in three types:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Large, small, and medium-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And use them only on bare skin, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	Sometimes another small tool, resembling the skin of an onion, is made according to this shape, with which one stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"and it is placed sometimes at the location where veins and arteries have been cut, and sometimes they are made according to this large form:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Some men's breasts swell when they begin to be corrupted, making them appear like those of a woman.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	And remain unsightly and swollen; whoever wishes to treat them must do so according to this shape from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape away the fat, dress the wound with healing ointment inside, then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch, and tend it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the breast hangs down and is soft due to its size, like that of women, then cut it open at two places on top through two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form:.b. up to line.g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat. Dress it as we have said for stitching and powders, and do what is necessary in tending until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it does not heal, or the incision is not fully made because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let him chew on the remaining flesh and fat, then clean it until it is sanitary.
des apostemes des asselles	swellings of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These hard swellings that appear under the arms are types of scrofulous tumors with hard edges, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the boil is emptied out, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it overnight, then remove all the cotton and heal it with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the swelling resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said in the section on scrofulous sores, and if the wound secretes pus, apply a cautery as we have said earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the bursting of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is cut and the skin above is sewn shut, abscesses often form; likewise when a vein bursts and there is an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	If it is known that it is for the artery, then the abscess will be long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel it with your two fingers, it feels like a pulling sensation.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	When it is for the vein, then it appears red and swollen.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it's foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is located under the armpits and groin areas or near the neck and many other places; it will be very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore one must avoid cauterizing with fire; and the one who is at its head must also avoid it, as well as the one that is caused by inflammation of the artery that can be seen through the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then perform an incision on the thighs, and carefully separate the artery from the tissue until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then place a needle underneath one side, and pierce it until it reaches the other side. Tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
