et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And you should apply this powder which will seal before the wound closes.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	The method of preparing the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	Take frankincense, one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Grind the mixture finely and sprinkle it onto the wound, then bind it tightly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	And then tie it securely, leaving it without being untied unless it swells.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For medicine is not removed until it is ripe.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"Sometimes this is also done with quicklime alone when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but before the air touches the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved, especially during summer, do not put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive oils or poultices made of barley flour and honey mixed with water until it weeps;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if bone fragments come with the wound and it is small, remove them with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	"of the wound on the neck"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between that and one on the head, except if the nerve of the neck or an artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave it alone and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be warm, like hot water washed in soft water and mixed with rose oil, and cabbage washed likewise in soft water, and other moist fomentations according to this manner, and moist poultices.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if wounds are deep and the boil is raised and full of pus, pierce it lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if an artery is cut, and blood flows copiously, ligate it, and tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the heart, and the blood vessels are preserved through which the flesh receives nourishment, then press the heart against the spine of the neck, and do not touch the neck but reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with poultices until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has gone into the bone, scrape it out.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are fragments of bone, burn them all away if you can, and those that you cannot have burned, let the wound fester until it is evacuated and its discharge tied off.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as described in its chapter
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds from spears or knives
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a wound from a lance or knife and it's deep, observe if any wind comes out of the wound as the patient breathes.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep but fresh with blood throughout, do not apply the powder at first or bind it too tightly, lest the blood return inward and reach the heart, killing the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, put some old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	So that there will be no spasm nor harmful trembling of the heart's breath.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see these good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat with compresses and other remedies until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot heal nor close, know that there is a fistula present;
si la cure si com on doit.	If the treatment is carried out as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a cut made by a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, then treat what is visible;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, sew it up;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, apply powder to it. And if it is pressed against the bone and has cut off pieces, then cleanse the wound and treat any exposed flesh.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not exposed, let the wound fester so that the extraction will be easier.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	Abdominal dropsy can be large, moderate, or small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	And sometimes a large wound allows the intestines or the nerve of the intestines to protrude;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the stitch is more difficult, sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because if one sets it too point by point, the intestines are not set properly.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Therefore, because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold and shrink more tightly, it is better to move the wound a little so that one can reposition the intestines in their place rather than elsewhere.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that an abdominal hernia occurs in four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The first two stitches occur in the abdominal stitch, and two other common stitches are found in other wounds of the body.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And moreover, they are more suitable for the abdominal stitch, and I will explain each one and make it clear.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestine sticking out, and there is little to reset, this is done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Wet a sponge or clean cloth in only warm water, or cook in boiling water with cumin and cypripedium and spikenard, and wring out the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this restrictive wine, and it is believed that [with] a sole [fish], to draw out the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, then mix the intestines with water or decocted aloe and mallows, for by this the entrance is eased somewhat;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it still cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to cauterize hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is believed to be that which makes the cut, and no one should cut there without great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the tool for splitting [it].
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If it does not cut within the curve and outwards, see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines stick out, then carefully put them back according to their natural shape into their proper place if you can, for this is important.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is located below the belly, you should make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if it is located below the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; also, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, make sure that the wounded part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus it should be arranged like this in large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, place what you have prepared, then use one hand gently to pull the whole wound with your fingers and bring together the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common method of suturing: take one or more needles according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave two spans from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the sinew, which is beneath the skin inside, until you make it pierced from that part, and bring together the two heads of the sinew in a group of four;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then tie a doubled thread around the needle at both ends, then bring together the two heads of the wound evenly, and then leave two spaces apart, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread knot as you did with the first needle, and continue to do so according to how many needles you need until all of the wound is bound;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, for thin needles cut all of the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	So that they must be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it can be closed;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then cut off the points of needles so they do not pierce the patient while sleeping, and place bandages or cloths on the points of needles to keep them in place until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this method of sewing with needles is more useful for small wounds, as it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second sewing method is common, and it involves bringing together the two edges of skin and the two edges of flesh with one needle using medium-strength thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And once you have pierced all three edges with the needle, pull it back towards where you started, like sewing cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And space each stitch about the thickness of a small finger.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This sewing method serves well, and I once sewed a wound that one man had in his belly, which was caused by a knife cut over a palm's length, and guts were protruding two palms' length, and the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestine afterwards when he had been feverish for 24 hours, and the wound healed up to 15 days, which I dressed, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged him to die, but it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with an ointment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and twice daily I put clean cotton on the wound and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways to stitch:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it from the outer part to the inner;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the heart directly, then lay the head of the cobbler's awl or cost where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the purpose of this stitch is that you sew like a furrier sews furs, leaving the awl on one side once and taking it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes precisely, is as follows: some people join the two parts naturally and apply one end of the thread to the other in this manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stick a needle into the nearby Chief Dou Mirach tendon and pierce it alone; leave both ends of the thread out.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle and pierce it from the outer part to the inner one, at both ends of the thread;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce each one again from the outer part to the inner one in two other Chief Dou Mirach tendons that are located on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most correct and common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen also says that one should suture the abdomen with two needles, each having thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew hides;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the ulcer is within the belly, the wound is harder to heal than from other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the air has moved it, then reset the intestines and the skin.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then place on the powder surrounding the flesh, and if the air has moved it, then place some ointment that is available, so that the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tie up the stitches, and let the edges of the incision and the middle close up;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would any other, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have medicines, then place cotton wool on it as soon as it begins to close up, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many cases where wounds are simple, there is no need for any other medicine besides this;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the main limbs, then it is necessary to wet light linen in warm rose oil or rose-colored oil, and place it around the angles and beneath the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or corruption in the bowels, and this happens often, then black wine suppositories are beneficial, especially if the corruption reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce it within, knowing that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The gut called 'jejunum' cannot heal when injured due to the thinness of its veins and the delicacy of its entire structure, as well as its closeness to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the herb jumps out of the wound, then replace it immediately like the intestine while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has turned green or black, then tie the place that is black so that no blood flows there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the tie, and place the two heads hanging down from the part below the wound up to its front for facilitating extraction when the herb falls out and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, for I saw that one man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which the digestion and wind escaped;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease until he was healed, with the wound soundly closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I feared that the patient might be suffering in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but there was no harm done, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And some experts said that when the intestine has a small wound, it should be tied up in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take large leeches, then gather the edges of the wound together, and when the leech has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it sucks them.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	And then he cuts off the head, and this holds so that it cannot be untied; then he adds another tremor afterwards in the same manner as before until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	And closes the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	These stones can enter the intestines without causing harm to the patient; and the intestines can be tied together with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this gut thread that is very skinned, and then tie to its head a thin twisted linen thread; then place the thread into the needle, and sew up the gut, and reset it in place.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this method of suturing tremors is not outside the scope of trust and hope
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, then there is no skill or health that can help except for delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know this: every wound or abscess, when it opens up, is universally called a 'fistula', and similarly when it is cut open and swells back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is, according to truth, broken and hard, white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also called like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear water, and at other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and at other times ample;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not clean and has no flesh, only appears by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, through the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or if there is too much water;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or if the place is putrid, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or if the medicine is not good in its care;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is of a pestilent nature;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow to digest and heal, and is naturally inflamed.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Where there are veins or bones
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal treatments in this division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now I must tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done through manual labor."
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the face, intestine, bladder, ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And there are some that come from the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and only labor and ignorance are responsible for them;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you are confident about its cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of brass or iron, and apply it to the fistula;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, search for it with a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends more easily around its twistiness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	If the fistula has many openings and you cannot examine it well by touch, then apply a clyster through one of the openings because moisture passes quickly from one opening to another, and this will cleanse it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then search for bleeding as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and how deep it goes. Ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press your hand on it, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you about, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the broken bone and rotted flesh that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Then treat it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep in its proper place, you must cut as deeply as possible, then put moistened lint soaked in hot water into medicine into it, up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine can corrode the excess flesh left at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I apply hot poultices of clean flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	If not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not trouble you in the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all corruption is removed, then treat with hot poultices of clean flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if not healed, return as before, knowing that you have not yet reached the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	So uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all corruption, then replace it in its proper place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	So there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small broken bone, and you can grasp it with pliers, then extract it using the appropriate instrument; but if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear, cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something irritating to cause rot on the wound and leave it until the spot around the bones is rotted away, then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it's a large bone, such as one in the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then close the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is much corruption and it reaches almost to the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	Then it must be cut all the way down to the corruption, and then cured until it is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	The young man was about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from an internal cause such that matter came to the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, without any apparent reason to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	Yet the doctors in their foolishness cut so much upon it that the abscess opened, and they dug out much matter, and it became a fistula, and many passages formed that continually emitted wind and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many doctors tried to treat it for about two years, but none of them were skilled in the art of hands, until I was called and saw his leg and the medicines they used, and what flowed through the passages with great force.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the young man's body became red, and he had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I then hurried, and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, which was found rotten and pierced; and the corruption had reached the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption besides that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And began to dress the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found that the corruption had continued into the bone itself, which I scraped out, and then closed up the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But still it did not heal until I cut around a palm's width of the bone and scraped it clean down to its marrow, then dressed it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it quickly became healed and sound, but the patient's weakness could not endure much more, and fear of death made me stop.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood occurred often, but he was entirely cured, and in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and it was well disposed and had no harm nor opposite in any way, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take linen, and bind it around the head of the exposed bone, and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another larger linen bandage over the first one and bind it above the flesh that is over the bone; then stretch the head so that you can pull out the corrupted flesh below and expose the flesh on the spot where you want the bone to be.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a splint or a board underneath the bone to move away the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	This must be done until one can see and feel all of the corruption, then it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted but not exposed, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose all of the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a splint underneath and stretch from one end of the corruption to the other, with the bandage being as long as the corruption is wide, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if corruption is at the joint, cut the corrupted joint, even if it contains bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there is no other choice but to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if corruption is at the wrist of the hand or at the ankle, that is very serious indeed; nevertheless you must investigate what caused this corruption.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And clean it in every way you can, but be careful not to harm any veins or nerves;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the incising tools and saws used to cut these bones are many, depending on the arrangement of the bones, their appearance from outside, their thickness and fineness, their length and shortness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore one must prepare each type of tool for its corresponding task.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you which tool you need to use, according to your knowledge of this art and the signs of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you consider the instrument with which you have need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head rots either from internal causes or from external ones;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that corruption with medicines but they do not help, then it is necessary to cut off that limb up to the point where the corruption reaches so that the patient escapes from death or from the greater harm of losing the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the sign is that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and after the blackening, the corruption spreads from limb to limb, spreading throughout the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	So hasten to cut it off; and if it is due to the bite of some venomous beasts like a sea scorpion or snake etc., then cut at the root of the two limbs, but do not let it come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, then cut it off at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it happens to the arm, cut at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the elbow, then death will occur, and no amount of medicine can save them due to the quantity of its poison.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And likewise when corrosion comes upon the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it happens at the first joint, then cut after the next joint
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it reaches the foot, then cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it goes up into the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it is above the knee, there is no other option but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the method of cutting off or cauterizing a limb is as follows: you should tie it above and below with ropes, extend one servant downwards from one of the ties and another upwards from the other tie, then cut away the flesh between the two ties using a wide knife until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cut or cauterize it and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy flesh, causing further injury or an abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs while you are operating, cauterize the area promptly using powders that constrain blood.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with an appropriate bandage and care for it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to one in great need:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a blackness appeared on him as if burnt by fire, and this corruption first came upon his big toe of the foot, spreading to consume the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he hastily cut off his foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And long afterward the corruption came upon the second toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied things that bounce back after cleansing his body, but the corrosion could not stop;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he asked me to cut off his hand, which I refused, for I hoped to repel the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also feared that if I cut his hand off, he would die, for the power of man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he became utterly despairing and returned to his land and hurried to have his hand healed, and he recovered.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Only this story is told for the sake of those who might otherwise act differently when there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No boil ever appears on tender flesh and remains so long that it collects a great mass of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts open and oozes out, leaving the spot empty like an emptied vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin on top is as delicate as the finest cloth and does not reach down to bone or nerve; such a disease is called 'clean' and is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it extends so far that it reaches down to bone and depth, then it is called 'fistula'.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And you must cut that skin all around, even if it is delicate, just like cutting a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not be concerned about its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	If you suspect that the skin is rotting but the decay is not deep and the skin is thick with flesh, then perform a cleansing enema like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Examine whether the breast is large and the belly that is emitting a foul odor; then administer an Egyptian-style cleansing enema made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take asafoetida, oil, and lead, in equal amounts, and cook them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take some of this according to your need, dilute it in water and honey, and administer the cleansing enema to the breast, closing the opening tightly;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is softened, and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes it is irrigated with water of ashes when this medicine is not present; take ashes of vinewood and pour water on them, then strain it, and use it for irrigation until you know that the breast is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then irrigate with water and honey mixed together with a little powdered lead.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you may irrigate with a mixture of honey and wine, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the blood airy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this and are confident that the breast is well cleaned, then irrigate with something that causes flesh to form there; take prepared tragacanth and mix it with rose oil in wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	When you use clysters of certain medications and ointments, about which I have spoken when treating ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening to the chest is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with an iron tool, and place a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, then you should only close it enough so that the clyster can enter, and if the opening that drips below is above, then cut it at or lower than its level.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the wound is deep, do not let flesh grow inside;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish, then arrange it in such a way that the wound extends to its lowest level; for when the wound is deep, do not let flesh grow inside and if you cannot cover the chest below as you wish
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	That the bow runs lightly downwards; leave nothing of the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take medicines that consolidate to put on the wound, and press onto the linen cloth that covers all the wound
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then push firmly against the opening of the wound with a cloth about one finger wide; press gently onto another cloth according to the size of the wound and place it on the wound to alleviate pressure from the bowels. Do not remove the outer cloth except once every few days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And that which is on the opening of the wound, often remove it to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels: whether it's venomous or little or much, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not; when your medicine has been applied in this manner, observe how it covers the wound opening, so you know that the chest is already healthy, and recovery approaches.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then relieve it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you dress the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast throws undigested bowel after many days, know that the breast has not healed yet.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people whose wounds take too long to heal with flesh, and others that do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested food suddenly jumps from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach has not emptied.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the stomach is slow to empty and feels distant, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in power, such as diaphoretic plaster, for it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphoretic plaster, and they make it with rose oil, and raise it with old wine equal in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	Then cook it and use it
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And if you cannot find diaphoretic plaster, or make it yourself better, take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, grind them, and powder them onto the honey while it is on the fire
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then wrap it in a cloth, and stretch it over the chest, and sometimes administer an ointment made from long pepper and celestial lily roots, which is also like wheat flour and centory.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And in the use of simples or composites:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them into powder, mix it with the honey I mentioned, and apply it as needed.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, know that the corruption has gone deep and is pressing on the bone, or on hard members, or on ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it's a fistula cure, as we have mentioned earlier
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A panaric is an abscess that develops under the nail of the little finger of the hand or foot, or sometimes in other toes.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is neglected as it ages, an abscess forms and spreads, eating away and digging down until it reaches the root of the nail, sometimes even destroying the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And corrosion reaches to the bone, causing foul-smelling pain; the thighs are two broad ones, and the color is yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If the treatment we have described does not help, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, and afterwards cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to prick and suppurate, you should put the edge of a knife beneath the nail that is pricking the flesh, lift it up, scrape off that delicate flesh lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with ointments until it is healed
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption reaches the bone, scrape it off and cauterize with fire, for as long as corrupt bone remains there, it will not heal
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the bone beginning to decay, scrape it off immediately as described above, then treat until it is healed
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is severe and painful, you should first cauterize it
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the big toe on an angle across, and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, as the patient would feel great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it does, then place something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the wound of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some people are born with the second joint [toe] completely fleshy, and sometimes there is cartilage where there should be bone, and occasionally there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, or their origin is in certain bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born with any knot of the thumb cannot move it, and he who is born at the joint of the thumb can sometimes move it.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut on one that is fleshy will be easy in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatu
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure
si te tien dou coper.	Hold it while cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those born with a knot on the back of the tendon, first carefully cut around the flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone at an appropriate angle, and then clean it until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come together at both sides come from birth, or from the welding of a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut that union so that the thumbs return to their natural forms
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two wet cloths or bandages soaked in rose oil so they do not join together
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you can place between two pieces of thin lead until the joint is well set as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocations come to any of his limbs with the palm, cut that fusion appropriately
des vils	Of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large vessels wrapped around, full of melancholic excesses, which come from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and this happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you must administer to him some times a purge of bile, and then cleanse him with the holy water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure by fire is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One way is to cut them off, and draw out the black blood with a feather;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is that you open the vein and draw all of it out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, rinse the leg with very hot water until the thick blood becomes subtilized, then press the leg of the patient from above the hip down to below the knee joint;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one, two or three places with a wide cut, then lift it up and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then the ointment, and instruct him to smear himself with meat juices mixed with black colophony;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are full, harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of him is done in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then place him in a bath, and raise the leg with warm water until it becomes red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, heat him by the fire, and then cut near the vein at the long part of the knee joint, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with an awl, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then place the probe beneath until it lifts the vein from the skin, and then lightly prick with an awl, then cut in another place three inches beyond.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape off the skin over the vein until it appears, then raise it with tweezers, as you have done before, and attach it to another clamp, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another incision, or several if needed, then raise it and cut at the two ends of the foot, then drag and raise it up to the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it inch by inch until it all comes out, then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot drag and raise it, then insert a needle with strong doubled thread into it, tie it and pull it out, place it under the skin, and turn your hand back and forth until it all comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure not to cut it, for if it cuts, you cannot pull or raise it, causing harm to the patient
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And once you have extracted all of it, place on the wound a wool pad soaked in vinegar and rose oil
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heal until he is sound.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and coiled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut it completely.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And draw it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts a vein is curved, and does not cut deep, so that it does not cut into the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And has a large curve, for if it were thin it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the public vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein enters into the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on dry land without moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it occurs in places other than the legs, and this happens due to rot that comes beneath the skin, like how worms and snakes enter between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude forth, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head opens, you must wrap a piece of cloth around it, from one and a half to two spans long, tie it, and let the cloth hang on the leg. And every time blood flows out, wrap the cloth around the iron and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap up the remainder, and do not cut near its root, so that all of it may be completely removed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh, causing an abscess and rot in the area, and bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be treated little by little until the top, and nothing should remain on the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein appears when treated from 6 to 8 palms long, or even up to 10 palms. A man once came to me whose was 10 palms long. When you cut it, insert a probe into the hole and pierce it all the way to the bottom so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter inside be emptied, and apply medicines at the site to prevent rotting for several days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the ankle or foot joint, and there are many holes from which blood flows;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Therefore, treat him as we have said previously.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	In our land this disease is called 'cattle disease'; it often affects oxen, and it is caused by a small worm that grows between skin and flesh. It moves throughout the body, ascending and descending, felt distinctly as it moves from limb to limb, leaving behind sores when it departs.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by corruption of certain bodily humors, such as worms, serpents, leeches, and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt about its severity, for when it reaches the head and enters the eye, it may cause blindness.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	This happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see one being treated or bled, one can only be sure that it is happening when the worm moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, tie the spot above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut into it and bleed it. If the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize the wound with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it causes is that it tears the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	If you see it coming near the eye's head, press down on the eyebrow strongly and then cut above it with fire.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And the patient should use bodily cleansing with dissolving medicinal solvents to remove harmful humors, and beware of putrid foods causing corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land 'vackir,' and it is a pain that comes into some limbs, which then moves from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a woman who was ill, and she uncovered her arm for me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And shortly after that, it swelled up to her shoulder like living silver moving from one place to another.
