li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain then left that spot and settled in her shoulder. Afterwards, it quickly spread throughout her body until it reached her other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she was always turning around her body as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how the member could move about so from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness behave in such a way."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Yet nevertheless, I had often seen many who seemed to want to move their limbs from one place to another, but I had never seen this in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, which is why that constraint appeared
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	but they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, having moist bodies and concealed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness being treated and the patient feels that pain which we have described, then quickly place the hand above and below, and then strike with a knife until that constrained wind emerges from its place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the spot;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you cannot see it with your eyes, then treat those that expel winds, such as fetid pills and pills of serpentine, etc.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and according to the places on the body where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The varieties of them are such that there are those with large points, small ones, hairy ones, and smooth ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And there are some with two angles, others with lengths, and still others where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	Those which fall upon any limb fall in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Either they fall onto a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When one falls upon any place on these members, the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	You must then be aware of extracting this arrow, as many deaths follow from various situations.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if these signs do not appear to you and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	The signs of an arrow striking the brain and piercing bone include: when the eye socket on top of the head jumps out, there is darkness and heaviness and restlessness in the eyes, redness of the whites of the eyes and inflammation of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps without cause, it runs from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps suddenly loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And moist white matter like flesh spurts from the wound, and it also appears as bruised flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If these signs appear to you, then take care of the case, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow striking the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were struck into something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like a bird, black blood comes forth, and coldness and cold sweat come on, followed by fainting;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know for certain that the man is dead.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a splinter that has lodged in the lung is when without any foam coming from the wound, phlegm rises up to the throat, and the patient changes color, sighs loudly, and seeks cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the belly, it is near the lower ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it causes great pain and sorrow and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter falls into the belly and no wind comes out through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for removal of the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, urine spurts forth and there is fever, and the patient feels great pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that wounds are deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members such as the face and neck and throat and shoulders and arms and back and thighs and legs and similar limbs are spared according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as happened to me once which I will tell you about so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at home to one struck by an arrow in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it out on the other side under the fat of the ear, without causing any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye under the skin, and the arrow was stuck, and I could only reach its point towards the wood, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was healed, and no bad outcome occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut the barbs, and carefully extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And drew out an arrow at home that had fallen into the belly, thinking he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And after he had passed 30 days, his condition did not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut upon the arrow, extracted it, burned it with fire, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man into whom an arrow has fallen on his back, and the wound has closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, without changing its natural position or causing harm to any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man into whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained there without causing him great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	And many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And an arrow was extracted from the neck of one of the king's men-at-arms, into whom it had fallen and which was slightly inclined towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely buried.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for to treat him three days after it had fallen.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought her with all my subtlety, yet I did not feel her at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I applied a plaster with atractive and digestive ingredients because the wound did not inflame;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and then the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster again the next day, and the wound closed up again, and the patient remained like that for a long time until he felt the arrowhead on the inside of his nose.
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a caustic medicine to the wound for many days until it was opened up and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrowhead sticking out.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then by applying this medicine on the opening of the wound, the head of the arrow became visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it was more than four months later that the wound opened up enough for me to insert forceps and pull on either side of the arrowhead, but I could not remove it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore I did not cease to refine and devise ways of tools until I obtained good pliers one day according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, so that I could pull it and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient became entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you can base your treatment on what I have not mentioned, for books cannot cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters compare even small things, and find new works and new tools when things are present or lacking according to the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows exit from the limbs where they are stuck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that jumps out where it enters is an arrow entering flesh, and sometimes jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh around it can be cut away, and then the dislocation should be reduced.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for a few days and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then if it jumps out; but if not, carefully cut around the whole joint until the place is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if an arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, some of the symptoms that I mentioned may appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	So do not pull it out but leave it until it becomes even after a few days, because if the arrow reaches such a place, death will occur.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not go too deep, and the patient remains for some days without bad symptoms, then try to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot come out thus, then apply warm poultices around it as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the joint until it is sound.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead has gone in deep so that one cannot see it, search for it carefully along its entire track;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with some suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, even though there is no bone, nerve, or vein involved, then widen the wound until it is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and draw out the arrowhead if you can; and if there are barbs on it that prevent its removal, then cut away the flesh stuck into both parts of the wound until you can remove the arrowhead by breaking or bending its barbs;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take care not to break the arrowhead as you draw it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot pull it out all at once, leave it until the flesh around has rotted away, and then pull it out; for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding is heavy and causes concern, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And guard against cutting into nerve or vein, and devise some way by which you might gently pull out the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or carefully;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And place the patient in the same position they were when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place them according to the signs shown to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that comes from another side, where some part of it is visible or the skin is swollen there, may be felt around about:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then cut until forceps can grasp it and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If one shoots now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand around until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and resume the extraction later until it comes out:
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the shaft of the arrow is there, burn all the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if the shaft falls off and you see that cauterizing is necessary, then apply the heated instrument such that the tip of the arrow enters into the heat of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then apply fire, and if the arrow is struck, insert the pointed instrument inside to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is embedded, you must cut all around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	If the arrow falls into the thigh or belly or bladder or side and it is near, you can reach it with your hand; if you do.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware not to touch the vein or nerve; then extract it and stitch the wound if necessary
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	"The shape of the tweezers used to remove arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is the illustration:"
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways for this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrow's feathers is like those of a bird, to attach at the tip of the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	"The shape of the tweezers for grasping and pulling out is like this:"
des voinnes dou cors communes	"for common wounds of the body,"
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one bleeds, among which there are sixteen at the head, namely
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The two temporal arteries located behind the ears, called the "doubles 'herb'";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries visible in the two temples
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins located at the inner corners of the eyes, called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	the vein located in the forehead
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein which is at the head of the nose.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two jugular veins on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins above the mouth's lips, which are called 'augueric'.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The commonly known veins in each arm are five:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first is the cephalic vein, which lies on the right side and is called 'vein of the head' by laypeople;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The second is called 'fast', it's composed of the cephalic and the basilica veins, and laypeople call it 'vein of the heart';
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilica vein lies on the left side, which laypeople call 'vein of the belly', it's above the flexor muscles and is the one visibly seen in the elbow pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvation vein lies between the little finger and ring finger with two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The first is beneath the curvature of the pouch on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein called 'nesse', which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The discharge from veins that are near the ears helps with old cataracts and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the discharge are such that you should raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then instruct the patient to turn their neck towards a vise until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent locations on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then grasp them with your thumb and index finger where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers, and squeeze gently;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand upstream along the vein, cut through skin and vein twice with a single stroke, and let blood flow out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then stretch and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for migraines, both acute and chronic, and for customary ophthalmia, and for watery tears flowing from the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of this healing are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient holds his neck so that both veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feel the pulse under your thumb, and then press firmly
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the heart upwards towards the vein on your index finger, place the lancet underneath it, and raise the vein upwards to cut it, just as you have done with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their dislocations and extractions at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the frontal vein is just as useful as that from the temporal vein for treating ancient face pains and headaches.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient twists their neck so much that the veins appear.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool called 'fosseur', of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein and press with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow out according to the amount you desire.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck and tie the vein until it stops bleeding, at most once with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, care must be taken that the bandage is not too tight.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And bind diagonally, for the bone is nearby and the bandage may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the temples helps with eye pain, and with headache, redness, earache, and face diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their injury is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it in some direction, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the wound, and if the wound is transverse, a bit long and wide due to the flame, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, it may sometimes break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then let blood flow until you need to, and then bind with cotton, binding it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Wounds from a vein near the nose are good for agues, and violent fevers, and facial diseases, like migraines and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the wound is such that the patient strains their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, and takes a subtle flame that is long, and sticks it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep at all; let blood flow according to your need, then bind it overnight, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The urine of two goats helps with the extraction of splinters and the beginning of measles, and aids many illnesses, including leprosy, corrosion, and hernias.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the properties of urine are such that the patient holds their neck under both [goats], as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat; then open the vein a little widely, then let blood flow temperately, as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then perform the other half on the other vein; then untie the bandage, and press gently around both veins so that the patient does not faint;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the washing of limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins above the lips helps with colds in the mouth, gum decay, cracked lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the treatment is to make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip up, and look at two veins, one on the right lip and one on the left, which are recognizable by their black color and the small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them or are uncertain, then cut the largest one on each side. Do the same for the two veins that are above and below, as this is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the washing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The treatment of the veins under the tongue aids after treating the cephalic vein, for strained throat and diseases of the eye and mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the treatment is that the patient sits facing you in sunlight, lifts their tongue up, and looks for a black vein under each side.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Health then both (joints), and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated are done so in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Either by pricking with a wide-bladed lancet or by incising with a sharp olive-shaped blade, known as an "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And are large and sharp according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the round flame is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary for opening the scalp veins that are full of visible thick blood, which contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the shape of the olive-shaped blade:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more subtly pointed and is for cauterizing the subtle veins where there is subtle citrine blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bloodletting from the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps those who are ill in the chest, throat, neck, and belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the bloodletter to perform the bloodletting correctly, and to beware of the artery that lies underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he strikes the artery and bleeding begins, he must stop it as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not be piercing, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic does not open visibly, you must remove it and replace it with another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any vein from it, or you sinew in place of it the vein within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And cut with the flame like a knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the sinew, then before you remove the arm, you must touch the location until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location beforehand, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the flame like a knife;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And be sure not to wound the artery when you see the location swollen, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid this then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see urine-like fluid coming out on top, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten yourself then, and place your thumb firmly downwards; once you have done so, remove your thumb if blood oozes out, as this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Tie the arm tightly, leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be in fear; do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	But if the blood does not ooze out and you faint, and no physician is present; then cut the artery if it opens, for the head withdraws.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fig bark, cut it open, and take half of it and tie it securely until the next day
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the bleeding stops, that's good
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, then treat it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have mentioned
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stainings are not considered serious in many cases due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The washing of the vein in mid-air helps by drawing blood from above the head and below the body; for it is composed of basilisk and celandine, as we have said
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the surgeon to warn him about the nerve that lies underneath, and if he cuts too deep, and finds the nerve, and inflames it, then the limb may be disabled.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve is often exposed, but in some men it remains hidden due to its fineness; therefore, you should heal it with the surgical hook before cutting.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And flee from the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, split it lengthwise."
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cauterization of the temporal artery helps by drawing blood away from the head and assisting with eye problems.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to cauterize with the olive-shaped flame or the myrtle-shaped flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one should seek the easiest place and not hesitate to try again if one fails at first.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the area may swell in some people when one fails at first, but it is of no concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of cauterization depends on your skill."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about health is that health is maintained foremost to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And health should be practiced in one of the three veins which are located on the arm:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely, the cephalic, basilic, and median cubital.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And bloodletting should be performed at the start of Lent, during autumn and winter after meals, when signs ofpletion appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	Bloodletting should be done on the first or third day, two or three hours after noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bloodletting administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but when necessary it should be done at any hour or time of day.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Children should not be bled until they are fourteen years old, nor women except during the fourth month after childbirth up to the seventh day.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	"Nor should one cauterize the elderly who have passed sixty years of age."
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to undergo bloodletting in any manner, they must first cleanse the bowels with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the bowels into the main limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He who is overly salty from foods, or drunkards, even if they are feverish, cannot be cured.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one desires to be cured after a bout of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, menstrual flow, labor pains, sleeplessness and fasting, or any loss of strength due to injury or illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the humors by eating and drinking appropriately, if you have that power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter a bath if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood and heal the vein around the third rib, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard against work, overeating, lust, and similar things that day
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be at rest and joyful, with the healer standing higher than the patient being healed. Then rub the arms twice or thrice, then loosen the belt in the middle, for when it is too tight or short, blood cannot flow properly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then he rubs the joint with his hands until the veins swell, which can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	He then moistens the burning forceps with a drop of old oil, places his left-hand thumb on that vein below the joint where he wishes to cauterize, ensuring that the vein is not empty or collapsed before striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like strings when cauterized, and some are so full of windiness that when the burning forceps is placed upon them, they withdraw at once and cannot be opened.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, then the wound will be too narrow, so the cauterizer must be wise in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	But if not, he should begin again a little below or above that joint, if the joint is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps abscesses will form there
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not put him in a bath, then continue the treatment if he wishes
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the hole is small, or blood flows thinly and you doubt whether it bleeds enough, then insert in that same hole all at once directly
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And do this quickly before the area becomes swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for often it happens that wounds are small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not continue the treatment and put on a little oil-lees, for it lightens the body of blood and is gentle in this place the lees of oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer oil-lees in each treatment of veins that you treat, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this same occurs with the head of the shoulder joint, when it is put back in its place
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so subtly lets the blood flow and disperses it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when the vein is not properly cauterized at the time of opening it and the incision is small, then hurry and apply a warm, moist sponge made from water and silk for about an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein has stopped, and if it remains in its place for a few days without any blackness or greenness, then there is no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see this, apply some aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, balm, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and swelling appear at the site of cauterization
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Therefore, place your hand on it, and if you find that the spot is soft to the touch when pressed, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Thereupon, take care not to place anything on what we have said, for by chance it may cut the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But use dry linen bandages to toughen the area, then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	"And draw from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood."
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	It is necessary for one who is full and bloated, and needs bloodletting, to make the incision larger, so that the flow of blood is wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite; it is necessary to bleed frequently and carefully, cutting across rather than pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of bleeding prevents loss of blood and damage to nerves, and is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body fails at digestion, it is necessary to give soft bread in juice of pomegranates.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, then draw blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before digestion soft bread in musk syrup, or in syrup of aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, then he must drink broth of meat and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for vein evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	"And if he wishes to empty one arm and bleed elsewhere another time, when he is weakened by much bleeding, it is necessary that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength."
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	"And whoever wishes to empty one arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong body, should bleed again 24 hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour."
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	"And whoever wishes to bleed elsewhere should bleed on the second or third day."
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	But he has much blood within his body which is already overheated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Therefore it is necessary to draw out a large quantity [of blood], and to widen the incision until it flows freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then when you have prepared all the conditions for digestion, and place your hand on the pulse while it digests, take care that the patient does not come in place of the pus, for this happens many times when the digester is careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And do not allow the hand to untie the bandages too quickly, nor let blood flow a second time when the incision is closed; press firmly upon it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, let him straighten his arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it be until the second time he recovers;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or else prick with the tip of fire until the frozen blood inside the vein comes out, then put some lint soaked in water on it and press lightly
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	"And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not compress it until the swelling has subsided."
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	"And if there is need to draw blood a second time, then bleed in the same vein or in another vein or in the other arm."
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	"The veins of the arm are bled instead of the cephalic vein because they are composed [of many small veins]."
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to heal is for the patient to put their hand in warm water until the joints are red
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately so that the vein appears well; then cauterize now across, not too wide nor too long
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the prick be large; and cauterize well near the joint of the hand; and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in warm water and let enough blood run into the water
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the blood of this vein is safer than all others, for there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood from the vein on the right hand's palm is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it should be done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Stretch out the hand, and place it in warm water until the vein swells enough to be visible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is crossed, and you cut along its entire length without hesitating, there will be no harm done.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not cut too deep, for nerves lie beneath all veins devoid of flesh. Then place the hand back in warm water if the blood is coagulated in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And once you have removed as much blood as necessary, then place oil and lint on it to seal it quickly, and do the same for each wound."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The urine from the left hand is good for treating mousse disease, and do everything as I have told you regarding the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The balm of the phoenix is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of menses, and disease of the loins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	The quality of this blood is such that when the patient places their foot in warm water and rubs it onto the vein until it disappears, they should tie above the ankle joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	This vein is located at the ankle, and many nerves pass over it higher up on the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Saw through then the bone where thicker it is, or at the ankle joint, whichever you prefer.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you saw through it above the foot, then beware of the nerves that are beneath, and saw it across as in cutting a stick.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be oblique
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to empty well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the sawing fails on the first attempt, then begin again a little higher up, for the place is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not fear damaging the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise to the shinbone of the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The scar of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its urine is beneficial for treating hip pain when it's due to hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of sawing it are that the patient enters into a bath, and is held above the ankle joint with four twists, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then saw through in all ways you can, and crossing
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better that you cut it off, for the place is dry, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, then take any vein of hers that opens on her thigh towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and draw out as much blood as you see fit, then untie the bandage, and place cotton over it and tie it tightly.
ele est maintenant sanee.	she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	removals by cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or earthenware, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping (ventosation) is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that is done without striking has two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with fire throughout, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cupping that is done by striking and bloodletting is performed on fourteen parts of the body, one of which is entirely on top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and another is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And two others are on both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the bloodletting cups of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the bloodletting cup on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the bloodletting cups between the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the bloodletting cups of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the bloodletting cups of the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And bloodletting does not draw blood except from the small veins that are dispersed throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, unlike bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be applied, neither by fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from excess, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it becomes necessary to perform bloodletting due to illness or custom, we will apply it once at the beginning and once at the end of each month.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need bloodletting, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And some find excess and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness before the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an inflamed tongue, and spew blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are also those who dream, and see in their veins blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month of May, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sweat of the forehead aids in relieving the heat that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to occur after all of the body has been evacuated.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this sweating is in place of the sweat from the forehead, and it is not necessary for those who are of cold temperament to use it, or those with a cough, as this causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore, old people should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often cauterize themselves become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping jar a little further down to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Sweating in the neck is equivalent to sweat from the head and back, and it is beneficial for tightness of the chest, splitting of the channel of the lung, coughing, andpletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And one must apply heat gently, for if it is applied too forcefully, it could cause injury to the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	And wind evacuations from the ribs of the neck are useful for headaches and eyestrain, migraine, strangury, and toothache pain, and they are in place of a purge.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the surgeon not to compress the artery nor cause blood flow during cutting.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	And evacuations below the chin are useful for mouth diseases and gum decay, and similar mouth ailments.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And they serve as substitutes for purging of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses caused by heat andpletion."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	And evacuations on the ribs are as useful as three veins in the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Instruct the surgeon not to proceed too deep, for the spot is devoid of flesh and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttocks is useful for hemorrhoids and illnesses below; it is necessary that the cupping glass be large and made of brass, so that it may draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	And it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Leg cupping glasses heal openly because they draw blood from the whole body and are useful for old pains in the back, sciatica, and the bladder; they also reset dislocations.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are placed on the two thighs and the two ankles; moreover, they weaken the body after prolonged use and cause dizziness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of placing the cupping glass is to place it first empty and suck temperately; then place it quickly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the area turn red and inflamed and appear the redness of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then burn it, and remove the cupping glasses, and take care with the arrangement of the body, for there are some who have thin flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to strike only once, then wide and somewhat deep cuts must be made;
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, then one must strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to draw out only a little blood, once will suffice.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish for much blood, then we repeat often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is dense, strike deeply, and stop when the heart has been suddenly pierced. This applies to those with thick skin and hard flesh who have narrow pores: you must anoint the places for cupping glasses with permeating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in place, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in joint, with mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one whose flesh is tender and has wide pores is treated, there should be no point of oil applied, but it should be washed afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucurbit water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very moist should rise using myrtle water, sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or water of the sun, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And one must not use a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he warm himself when he must be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware those who are being treated have hot temperaments, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then they should take cold things like pomegranates, endive, lettuce with garlic, and similar foods.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat pork meat, castrated ram meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have cold complexions should take syrup of honey and moderate aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and eat roast pork and roast pork meat and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day when he evacuates, he should drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And some people should be given treacle or muscat three times before evacuation, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the blood be subtly drawn, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are placed without wounding are those placed on the liver, womb, gout, belly, face, back and thigh, for these members do not tolerate being wounded above them, and they are only used to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when a woman is in labor.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity in the limb, as we place cupping glasses on the abdomen and cheek to reduce the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves pain when there is a stone or gallstone, as it can attractively remove by its power through suction the stone, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and likewise it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire together, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of the lungs, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have around the middle a small hole, like that for a needle, made of brass, soft before use so that it does not wound the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And it should have in its midst a crossbeam of bronze or iron, to place an enclosed candle upon, and they (the candles) should be both large and small according to the illnesses and the ease of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and for the thin they are different from those for the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cupping glass upon the limb:
