empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Insert the candle made of wax or linen, and place it within the cupping glass across the crossbeam that is inside the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass where it cannot burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it upon the limb, and ensure that the opening we spoke of is above, so that when you want to, steam can escape, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And again insert the linen wick as before, and keep relighting it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore in the cupping glass prepared for pleurisy with sharp pain, it has no crossbeam or opening; and it is only heated when filled with water, then placed upon the limb.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups cannot be applied except in limbs where one cannot place them due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in areas devoid of flesh, such as the knees or nose, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And its usefulness is that when you find suction cups that are clean and bright with no signs of use, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in warm water until they are swollen and have nothing inside.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then disinfect the vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the cups on.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and dropping, if it is a place where one can put a suction cup, then put one on, for this is very useful afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the limb gently, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the wound heals too quickly after bleeding, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the blood congeals.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the blood is multiplied, apply ground vitriol or gauls ( oak galls ), or similar substances until it coagulates.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you can place half a handful of peeled beans on the wound and leave them there until they adhere to the wound; it will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins do not want to take blood, rub fresh blood on the wound and stick a needle into it until blood flows out; then apply the cloths so that they adhere once they sense the blood.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see them full, powder some alum and salt ground together or ashes on top of them; they will now clot.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians scorn this chapter because they have never seen any of the old books nor read any letters concerning it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge is scarce in our land, for I found none of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have learned the knowledge, and through experience, and through my life's practice.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are arranged, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of words and chapters where the wise puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are skilled know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or crushing occurs in anyone, you should hasten to bandage the patient on both sides, except if there is anything preventing it entirely, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the time is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And drink cold drinks, that is to say, cold foods, and bird meat and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you doubt a hot abscess, or an expansion of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to their first good governance which they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the sick person with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, milk, wine, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment muscles are rebuilt more quickly and the fracture heals sooner."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the elderly and infirm cannot be properly reset or mended according to their natural state due to the weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But if there is no cure, reset and bind with thick bandages the broken bone tightly until it heals as before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not let any point of its work remain undone, for this reason they must be nourished with plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the arm or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that fractures can occur."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are fractures that go to the bone and others that do not affect the bone, such as cutting off the tip of a quill for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is fracture with wound, and fracture with just a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings back into place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	A break in the bone is recognized by the twisted appearance of the limb, and it can be clearly felt by touch when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting or sound on touching, nor does the patient feel great pain, then there is no break present.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may well have curvature, or cracking, or minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand, but apply the medicines that are mentioned below and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which goes into the air, and consists of two disjointed parts, must be set evenly before a swelling comes.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if a swelling soon comes, let it remain for some days until the swelling is pacified;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it evenly with the movement you can easily and gently make, for know that the restoration of this one is easier than those which have pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then bind it as it must be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, stretch them out with two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are dislocated, you should reset them all with all your strength in their places with the movement you can make, and ensure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And join the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems not to be properly set:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If you raise it nicely and do not pull it too hard or press too much, as those who bring about heat and contraction to the limb through their practice of cautery, as we have often seen:
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if it feels any pain, then it is not set properly, and you must place it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And make sure it is placed correctly, so that there are no twists when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	The qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken limbs are diverse in size, length and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	Because there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	therefore, soft and fine linen cloths should be used to wrap them.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are large, such as thigh and leg
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage encases the entire large limb evenly, and presses it equally on all sides so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap it around with light pads, three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on all the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less so that the break can move away from the break a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and slowly loosen the bandage bit by bit until you grasp most of the healthy part, then take another bandage and wrap it around again on the broken limb.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break and tighten it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the limbs wads of linen or rags, so that it is entirely even; then bind everything above with bandages, and then place well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something that cools and draws out the heat of the abscess, and reduces swelling, leaving it thus for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then press down on your dressings, using something about half the width of a large cane, properly trimmed, or wooden battens used for stakes, or palm ribs, and they should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But the dressing placed on the fracture must be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And it should also be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then press down on the dressings just as you did with the first binding, then tie above it evenly, just as in the first binding over the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	Further above is narrower; suddenly less.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the threads be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their sutures from twisted linen ropes, and this is a great error, because the suture cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two spaces between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the stitches after they were placed in the healthy places, then put pieces of linen or wool gauze underneath them so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to stitch all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	But when the limb is large, you should not put in stitches before after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your sureness of the heat of the abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here you will find the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And take the flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, use it for setting fractures in various positions, especially for women and young children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take incense and ladanum and mullen and asafetida and gum arabic and magnesia, nine parts.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, five parts.
alechil VIIII З.;	aloes, seven parts.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And grind it into powder, then mix with egg yolk
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the constitution of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take magnesia and malva (mallow), nine parts each.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, seven parts each.
acaice VI З.;	acacia, six parts
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	bolus armeniac (arsenic trioxide), ten parts, grind well and mix with vinegar or egg yolk, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and bones out of their places, and alleviates the pain that ensues, and prevents bone growth and breaking:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, wetting it with hot water and oil, then apply to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore but is good for soothing a hot boil and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way of setting broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and common mallow leaves, grind them together to make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to soften the remains of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take equal parts of the following:
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them together and mix with wine. If the limb is inflamed, mix it instead with coriander water or plain water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger plaster for when a hard abscess comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take equal parts of the following:
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them together and mix with saltwater, fresh water, or wine according to the warmth of the limb and its restfulness.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should only apply on the broken limb for restoration a cerate made of wax and oil, nothing else more. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen agrees that one should apply on the broken limb for restoration dry things somewhat warm, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way for poultices that are good for wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take an equal amount of mullein flowers, chicken feathers or human hair, and valerian root. Grind them together to make a poultice.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then after dislocating it a little later, take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	unless it remains dislocated for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain or itching comes on, without rest or swelling, then act quickly and dislocate it again, removing the obstacle immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light cloth and a damp sea sponge, dip it in water, and lift it to the spot until the itching ceases and the pain is eased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, dampened with water or rose oil, and bind it tightly until you are sure of having produced a warm abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and once the pain is gone, then begin the gentle binding again, with a little more pressure this time, but not as strong as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue thus until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the swelling is hot and red and painful and swollen are all gone, and you need plaster and binding again, then begin again gently, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if there comes to the limb none of what we have said, then do not dislocate it except after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes leave it for twenty days, as is seen, until the fracture heals and the union of flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then tighten more than before, and let the flesh grow thick, as I have said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see that the place dries out more than necessary, know that no healing will come from it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm water compresses all the times you dislocate it, and this should be done every third day, and loosen the bandage a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Thus healing of the limb is accelerated, and swiftly corrected what foolish doctors do, who reset the limb incorrectly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is evil, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing else but doubt and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of diverse kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures there are, and various shapes, and their causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, and the collarbone breaks the entire bone up to the shoulder blade which is beneath the bone, like an axe or log;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And therefore this type of fracture is called "haiche.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "absolute.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And in these two fractures the wound may be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	"And if there is percussion that strikes in, or cuts into, the collarbone of stone, or from falling onto stone, or other similar ones."
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	"And if there is a persistent fracture, approaching close to the membrane that is under the bone or over it, and this wound is large or small."
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	Also there is a fracture where the wound enters the bone so subtly like a hair, and the split is small; therefore this fracture is called "capillary.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling or similar cause, and pushes in the piece of bone downwards, causing the place to be raised like a roofer striking slates on a roof;
si entre li piere dedens.	If the stone enters within the kidneys.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it occurs with all types of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	I will speak about it in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	"And we know all kinds of fractures by their retraction upon them, and detection through probing, and by the corrupt flesh that is upon them."
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on top, then the fracture opens black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of accidents to the patient. And if you see no evil accident such as vomiting of bile and loss of consciousness and extension and paleness and intermittent fever and eyes coming out black and red and other signs in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any astonishing accident and hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, if it is in wintertime, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summertime, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the flesh under the bone becomes corrupted and the accidents that we have spoken of occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut into the broken part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And take the patient's head and uncover the bone in all possible ways, and do so gently according to the shape of the wound; if blood flow or a hot abscess occurs when uncovering the bone, help as necessary; then fill the place with wool moistened with rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the hot abscess is appeased, and ensure that there is no further bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to remove around the bone; this can be done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is thus: you cut narrowly and straight ahead, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And another manner is thus: you have many cuts of diverse shapes, some narrow and pointed, others wide and made of soft iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, you must encircle it with a drill before administering cuts with awls, ensuring they do not pierce too deep and go beyond the bone's soft part; above the point there should be a margin or circle that prevents the point from protruding beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have many such awls so that each comes into its proper place on the edge of the bone, thus allowing you to have awls for all kinds of bones.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three manners of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities for drilling around a broken bone are that you place the drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is drilled through.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then move the cautery elsewhere a little later, and do so all around; then cut with the scalpel the space of bone that is between the pores, doing this more subtly and gently than you can, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as tongs, forceps.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And ensure that you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, then you must reset the fragment that remains of the bone with another tool resembling a scalpel, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other scalpel;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with one of your tools.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of work is that which Galien speaks of, which is more cautious;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and tie it very tightly, that is his order.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture appears open, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place underneath the head of this lens-shaped chisel, its shape is shown here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side only; the bone is sharp on both sides so that the cut is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer so that you gently tap the bone all around; and be careful of the tissue underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adherent to the bone, remove it gently, for one can do so safely without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the tissue and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces remaining, then remove these roughnesses using a fine file that you should have in various quantities to prepare each area according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then use coarse files first, followed by finer ones until it is smooth enough.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other capillary incisions and subtle fractures, you must bring about closure according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is not something easily answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinew is exposed, you must take one cloth of linen according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over twice or thrice, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you can, so as not to strain the sinew, then apply the other ligature on top and do not pull too hard until it touches the wound only.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it thus for one or two days until the abscess is reduced, then untie it and apply medications such as lily roots, walnut flour, frankincense powder, and aristologus, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Grind these ingredients into a powder, apply it to the wound, and repeatedly apply warm remedies without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is always clean, leaving no ointment on it or allowing flies to gather on it, for when flies congregate on the brain cloth, they will corrupt and inflame it, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when one places something corrosive on the sinew, it will necrose above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, beware if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, that it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness appears on the outside due to the medication applied, which has such virtue, then you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil and mix it with one cloth, and place it on.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him in various ways until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the kneecap above are broken, or just one by itself, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilage and does not break, except when struck from behind or twisted, after which it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must place your little finger or middle finger on the hole of the kneecap and push the break evenly with your index finger from behind until the kneecap returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain because of your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the shoulder and the arm cannot be moved into place, you should put it against the head of a slightly thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, then repair it thus, and hasten to restore on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation is subdued, then wrap the head of the newly broken bones with linen cloths.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind the other part separately, if there is a fracture there
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the hollows of the newly broken bones.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say one must soften the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem good to me that this is right; rather, they should be moistened in a mixture of egg yolk and mill dust
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the bandage on until the bone is solidified and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of bandages, and a soft cloth around them; if the break holds and the patient suffers less.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Do as you see fit
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the shoulder while you are working on it, put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil or a little diacodium upon it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not appear, then apply a plaster made of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then apply light compresses, but do not tie it tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture is small and broken into many pieces, then extract it with appropriate tools, then sew up the break and treat with wound healing plasters and ointments as appropriate.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside it, then cure it with tenting, and apply splints of lead until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Regarding the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured underneath and there is no wound on the outside, and the break is only on one side with no other fragments inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your two index fingers into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, put your right hand's two index fingers into the mouth and gently push the fracture in place with the other hand, applying equal pressure.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is offset by two parts, you must provide traction on both sides to ensure that it is aligned evenly.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movements of the teeth occur, or a fracture, then tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place over the broken jaw a dressing, and place over that a double bandage.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the bandage a well-made large compress or an equal length and width piece of leather according to the jawbone, tying it at the mouth where you can reach, and instruct the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure has changed, then untie it on the third day, and then reposition what was shifted.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place a plaster over it made from flour ground with abundance of egg or barley meal, after removing the dressing.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a light linen over it, and if the plaster dries and there is no change in the patient's condition, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling occurs, use the treatments we have mentioned many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both fracture and wound together, check whether any piece of bone has been broken off.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the bone fragments are very small, suitable tools are necessary for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After removing all the fragments, if there is no more remaining, sew up the wound if it is large and apply healing plasters until it is healed.
de la forcele	Regarding dislocations of the joint
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The arm breaks often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Either it is broken and dislocated at two places with fragments, which is the easiest to reset;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure for fractures without wounds is: have two assistants so that one can hold the arm which feels the fracture.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture evenly on your two hands so that its shape is correct with no deformity or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round roll of cloth or wool, whose size suits your needs;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And they raise and straighten the arm, holding the spear steady with your hand so as to set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	"And if you cannot draw the head of the arm forward because it is too deep, then the patient must lie flat on his back and place under the shoulder a medium ear-pad, and push the shoulder backward until the bone of the fracture rises."
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then align the fracture with your two fingers, and if you find it displaced, then you must cut upon it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and carefully draw the fragments together, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then cut one of the incisions that you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but make sure this instrument is placed underneath the arm, for fear of cutting the sinews.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should resemble a spoon and not be raised, and be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should have two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you drew together the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that there is a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small or you doubt whether there is heat in the abscess, cover the wound with lint and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	"And if hot swelling comes, wet a piece of linen in rose oil and hyssop and wine, and put it on."
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and cuts, is that you put on the bone the plaster made of mill dust and egg white, and place light dressings on top, and put a splint under the limb if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage, about a palm's width, then place the doubled cloth on top of the dressings and plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a narrow strip of linen about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the strip on the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, under the healthy limb, and under the injured limb.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And tighten each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the break securely, and you can clearly see that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then wrap it again every day, and when the ligatures loosen, then tighten it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on his back, placing a small pillow under his shoulder while he sleeps to lift the shoulder joint upwards;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	So ease the breakage of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, tying the arm to the neck if necessary, and not untie it until twenty days have passed, unless some misfortune occurs;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then restart the treatment, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it thus until it is healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it will be restored within twenty-eight days for most people, though it may take less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	"Regarding the fracture of the shoulder"
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It can happen that the broken or dislocated shoulder does not return to its proper place, and cannot be put back into place except by touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	So arrange it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in every way that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then place on the spot powder from a millstone mixed with plenty of egg whites and light lint, and cover it with a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place over it a wide and thin bandage, slightly wider than the shoulder. If there are any hairs underneath the bandage on some part of the shoulder, then fill that area with linen wads so that the bandage lies evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then fasten it firmly with a large bandage all around so that the bandage does not move from its place. Check the dressing each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time he moves, tighten it again and ensure that the bandage remains evenly placed if it has shifted from its position. Have the patient lie on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these days are completed, then untie it, but be careful, for it is not bone that easily goes out of joint again.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	"And if a piece of bone sticks out in front and not under the heart, then cut it off, and do what we have said regarding the fracture of the arm to appease hot inflammation."
de la brisure dou pis	"Regarding the fracture of the wrist"
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	Sometimes the flesh is broken in half, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the joint.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downward and the patient feels great pain, faints, falls down, and sometimes vomits blood. The horse's jaw opens at the broken bone and they can be felt well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is done by having the patient lie often on their back. Place a cushion between their shoulders, then press their shoulders together and bring the ribs of the two sides gently towards each other with your hands, carefully arranging them so that the bones are properly aligned.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place compresses and bandages on the fine salt siphon, or another light wood, wrap it in a cloth, and lay it upon the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And bind the tie firmly behind, and tighten gradually, and check each hour to ensure it is secure, and if it loosens, then tighten.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it becomes necessary to untie it, due to corrosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or an abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the compress, and apply remedies as needed.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the compress, and tighten it until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	"Regarding the fracture of the ribs"
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that a break of the ribs occurs only in large places after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only because they are smooth.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one feels it well during examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you align the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break of the ribs inclines towards the inside, then the patient feels very great pain and sharpness, also like pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it hurts like pricks, and suddenly he vomits much blood, which is of great seriousness; the ancients have spent much effort on this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"And there are those who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly to push the fracture outward."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"But we do not do this, lest boils come if they have not already done so."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"And if it comes to this, then heal it."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one should put cupping glasses on the spot to suck strongly, which seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	still, there is doubt that the cupping glass will draw out the excesses to the place due to its weak attraction.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And some said that one should cover the joint with moist wool soaked in hot oil, and apply bandages between the ribs to make the binding even. Then it should be treated with the cure for pleurisy, meat, and medicines."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the bone piercing the lung, and there is doubt for the patient, then one must cut upon the spot of the broken rib, and put an instrument underneath to guard the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone and draw it out gently, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and dress the wound with emplasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a boil suddenly comes, then put warm woolen cloths soaked in rose oil on it, and place them on the spot;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the boil's location with what is appropriate for boils, and let it lie continuously on the affected side until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	"Regarding the fracture of the neck"
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a bone in the neck breaks, and rarely does it lean;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And if this happens to someone and you want to know whether he will recover or not, take note if his hands are softened, swollen, and numb, and he cannot move or extend them. When you prick them with a needle, he should not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many ways. If he moves his hands and feels well when they are pressed or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will recover if care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healed or not, take care if the feet are softened, and if the limbs have accidents that are beyond control, and wind and gas are expelled without volition;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is placed on its belly, expulsion occurs without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back wanting to mount [a horse], then he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Such things are deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	So do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if there is a hot boil, you should apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to the spine until it is soothed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then apply one of the comforting and drying emplastes, tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone dislocates, then cover the heart with it.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Remove the bone, then approximate the two lips of the wound if it is large with one stitch, then dress it with ointment around the flesh until it heals.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the 'cow's knee', then place your left hand's clenched fist into it and align it with your other hand with all your strength, then apply the emplaste and splint if necessary.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then bind it, and if there is any dislocated bone, set it back in place, remove the bone, and dress the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It can happen that the hipbone is broken, and if this happens, there will be a little lessening of movement in the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And cut with length, inclining towards the partition, causing pain to the patient at that place, prickling, and swelling where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the reduction is thus: stretch your hand upwards until you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which part is broken and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the break is only at the top, then set that break even with it being in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or slopes inward, make the patient lie on their stomach so that you can easily see and treat the fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And once you have set it even, then place a splint on top, then place a wooden or bone wedge on it and hold the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and tie beneath the ribs until the binding is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And tell the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess has subsided, and then place what we have mentioned above;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the reduction, holding it as necessary if there is no bad complication.
et c’est li maniere.	And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder blade
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder blade is what lies between the elbow and the head of the shoulder. If it is broken, then it should be reset according to one of these two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of which one method is that you take a wooden splint, thick with groats, shaped like this:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two heads with two bands, and fasten them upwards; then have the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then place the broken arm on the splint until it reaches the axilla, and is held in a concave wooden support; then hang something heavy from it, or have the minister press it downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then the physician should bring the break level with his hands together until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his hatchet-blade, and he holds his hand to his neck, then orders two assistants: one takes what is above the break in his hands, and the other takes below at one link, and each extends to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then restrain the sinews beneath the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the helpers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you should put one band under the axilla and the other towards the elbow, under the break;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the fracture is towards the cost side, then one must gently place the splint without effort, until the fracture is level on the site and on the cost.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the fracture evenly as it should be, and bind it, so that no swelling may come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if swelling comes quickly, do not bind it until seven days have passed; then place damp linen soaked in hot oil rose, until the swelling is eased.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then bind it, and the way to bind is thus: place the bandage on the fracture, then bring the arm close to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And place the bandage, and bind it on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in line with the stars, unless something prevents it or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use stars; place a larger and stronger star on the fracture, with two spaces between each star, and let each star be so large that it passes three fingers beyond the fracture on either side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then press on the joints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about fractures.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the settling of the joints and their restriction, as we have said, when you reset the broken limb, and if you doubt that the hot abscess will heal, let it be until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then examine each site every three days to ensure that no itching or swelling occurs where the bandage was placed, so that the limb does not suffer injury due to being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the dislocation, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	And place a flat pillow filled with even wool under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night to ensure that the position of the broken limb does not change or the bandage become loose.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If the patient is cured through medical knowledge, then give them the food that we have mentioned previously, but grind it first.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And when they begin to recover, it should be coarse.
